Explanation of Silk Factories' Opposition to Public Weight Verification 127

Reply from the Bureau of Commodity Inspection to the Silk Factories Trade Association

Reasons for Opposition from Some Businesses Are Not Justified

Reply from the Shanghai Bureau of Commodity Inspection to the Committee of the Silk Factories Trade Association: "In response to your letter of September 21st, where you state that some silk factories have written to express their losses due to weight discrepancies and requested an emergency meeting to discuss solutions, a meeting of representatives was convened on the 18th of this month to propose suspending public weight verification starting October 1st. This has been duly recorded and forwarded. Upon investigation, the Bureau previously provided a clear explanation of the causes of weight discrepancies in a letter dated the 8th of this month in response to your association's inquiry, which should have eliminated the need for further explanation. However, we understand from your recent letter that some silk factories still do not have an accurate understanding of the public weight discrepancy issue. Therefore, to avoid repetition, we provide a detailed explanation once more. The Bureau, as a national commodity inspection agency, should advocate for fair trade on the international stage and cannot be biased towards either buyers or sellers. If raw silk is humid, it contains more moisture, disadvantaging the buyer. If it is dry, it contains less moisture, disadvantaging the seller. Public weight ensures an accurate measurement regardless of weather conditions. Therefore, the public weight system must be adopted for verifying the weight of raw silk. This is recognized worldwide and is a national policy. The Bureau is implementing orders from the Ministry and cannot arbitrarily change them, nor can anyone with personal bias lightly discuss them. As for the loss of weight, some silk factories have repeatedly claimed that they have very valid reasons. However, from a logical perspective, this is not justifiable. Whether or not there is a weight discrepancy in raw silk inspection depends entirely on the water content (汀) in each factory and the dryness or humidity of the weather. If the water content is sufficient and the weather is dry, the public weight after inspection will be more than the net weight, as evidenced by factories like Baotai Silk Factory, where the public weight of their raw silk is consistently higher than the net weight. If the water content is low and the weather is humid, the public weight after inspection will be less than the net weight, resulting in what is considered a discrepancy. In reality, the loss is due to the removal of excessive moisture that should not be present in the silk. Since the removed moisture should not be in the silk, how can the so-called loss be considered a genuine loss? Even if we disregard this, considering the advantages and disadvantages, factories tend to lower the water content during the summer months when workers find it difficult to bear the heat, exacerbated by the humid weather, resulting in weight discrepancies after silk inspection. As the weather gradually dries up in autumn, the water content gradually increases. According to statistics from the 15th to the 23rd of this month, a total of 824 bales were inspected, with a net weight of 82,465 catties and a public weight of 82,581 catties, 126 catties more than the net weight. If the beginning of autumn is like this, the situation in winter can be imagined. The period when weight discrepancies are seen due to hot weather and low water content is only about four to five months. During the remaining time, not only will there be no loss, but the public weight should be more than the net weight. Gains and losses balance out, so where is the loss? Furthermore, if silk factories do not seek excessive moisture and add sufficient water content during the silk reeling process, it can make the silk's color bright and clean, the pulling force strong and resilient, and reduce thread breakage, thus improving the quality of the silk and increasing its value, which is of great benefit to the silk factory. After the Bureau opened the raw silk inspection facility, the elimination of losses due to foreign firm weighing and other malpractices has resulted in annual benefits exceeding one million. Silk merchant leaders have stated this repeatedly. Where is the overall loss? The opposition to public weight by silk factory businesses is tantamount to abandoning their own interests. Why not give it some careful thought? Foreign merchants aim to profit from their transactions. Silk factory businesses claim that public weight causes losses, but at the same time, they say that foreign merchants still do not recognize public weight. If public weight is truly beneficial to the seller and detrimental to the buyer, why would foreign merchants, who are not foolish, not recognize a fair and impartial public weight system and instead prefer using the net weight, which benefits the seller? This is logically incomprehensible. The Japanese silk industry was originally behind ours, but due to the concerted efforts of the government and the people to study and adapt to the trends, it has soared ahead and far surpassed our country. If silk factory businesses are unwilling to accept inferiority and want to compete with strong neighbors, they should exhaust all their thoughts and efforts to gain the world's trust through legitimate means. Only then can the silk industry have a chance to turn around. If they cannot be pioneers and are unwilling to adapt to global trends, clinging to old habits without changing, they will only be eliminated. How can they compete with the world? The public weight system is sufficient to correct unjust gains from excessive moisture in raw silk and protect the interests of those with less moisture. It can be adopted in any country. Why is it suitable for Japan but not for China? The Bureau would like to further explain to those who say that public weight is suitable for Japanese silk but not for Chinese silk: Japan is the leading producer of silk in the world, followed by our country. Italy and France produce very little. Currently, countries like Italy are using public weight. How can it be said that only Japan uses public weight? The Bureau's public weight inspection facilities are designed to handle over a thousand bales of raw silk per day, based on peak silk market conditions. Currently, the silk market is slow, so capacity exceeds demand threefold. Inspection will not be delayed. Delays in ship schedules are due to factories failing to prepare in advance according to the specified dates. The Bureau cannot be held responsible. If Chinese silk merchants want to develop foreign trade, they should not only improve quality and increase silk cocoon production but also adopt scientific management methods to streamline factory operations, save labor, increase efficiency, reduce consumption, and improve profits. Instead of focusing on these tasks, they are solely focused on competing for unfair moisture content to gain undeserved benefits. What kind of thinking is this? Is this what is expected during the era of national revolution? Members of your association, leaders of Shanghai silk merchants and members of the Righteousness Committee, also served as members of the Bureau's Raw Silk Inspection Preparatory Committee, participating in the decision to adopt the public weight system. It is hoped that you will maintain your initial support for the government's commodity inspection policy and explain the aforementioned points in detail to the dissenting silk factories to avoid further misunderstandings. This year's Jiangzhe cocoon harvest was poor, and factories have been suspending operations one after another due to insufficient raw materials. Some people are now trying to use the suspension of operations to coerce the government into maintaining a public weight system that ensures fair raw silk trade. Wouldn't that make them a laughingstock to the world? Members of your association, with a clear understanding of the modern silk trade trends, should not support this proposal. It is hoped that you will guide them well and avoid bringing trouble upon yourselves. Regarding the inability to justify the opposition to public weight by some silk factories and the raw silk inspection public weight system being a policy set by the government that the Bureau cannot arbitrarily change, nor can it submit opinions based on a lack of understanding. If some silk factories insist on their views, they should directly submit them to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for review. This is the reply to your association. We hope you will take note."

Incident of Dutch Citizens Insulting a Chinese Woman 128

Telegram from the Overseas Chinese Association to the Central Government

The Shanghai Overseas Chinese Advancement Association sent a special telegram to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission of the Central Government in Nanjing and the Ministry of Education regarding the incident of the first and second mates of the Dutch ship "Tjisedane" forcibly molesting Ms. Xiao Xin'an, a Chinese teacher hired by the Huaqiao Peide School in Ambon Island, Dutch East Indies. The telegram read: "To the esteemed Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, today's newspapers reported that Ms. Xiao Xin'an, a teacher hired by the Huaqiao Peide School in Ambon Island, Dutch East Indies, boarded the "Tjisedane" of the Java-China-Japan Lijn shipping company on August 14th. Before the ship reached its destination, she was repeatedly molested by the Dutch first and second mates. When Chinese passengers on board questioned the captain, he colluded with the ship's doctor to hastily diagnose her as having a mental illness. According to Ms. Xiao's own account of the molestation, the evidence is conclusive. The fact that the ship's doctor and others are trying to shirk responsibility suggests that they have been molesting Chinese women traveling to the Dutch East Indies for a long time, taking advantage of their silence. Although the incident has aroused sympathy and support from the Chinese community in Makassar, we are concerned that under the shadow of imperialism, it may not achieve any results. The association believes that this incident not only insults Ms. Xiao but also our entire nation. Therefore, we urgently appeal to the Commission to request the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to lodge a serious protest with the Dutch government and the consul in Ambon Island. If the Dutch government indulges in such actions, we request the Commission to consider further measures and not make any concessions to prevent similar incidents from happening in the future. This is to prevent Chinese women traveling abroad, especially those hired as teachers in overseas Chinese schools, from being apprehensive. If this case is won, not only will the victim's grievances be redressed, but our entire nation can also vent its anger. In anticipation, we await your instructions with utmost urgency. The Shanghai Overseas Chinese Advancement Association respectfully submits."

Second Report on Epidemic Diseases from the Quarantine Office 129

The National Maritime Quarantine Office of the Ministry of Health released its second report on cholera and plague yesterday: (Cholera) There are still several new cases of cholera in Shanghai every day. Out of the 49 people reported in the first report, 4 died. Since then, 42 new cases have occurred, with 6 deaths. From August 28th, there have been a total of 87 cases of cholera, with 11 deaths. Among those infected with cholera, several came from Suzhou and Hangzhou. In one family, all members were infected within five days. The government is currently investigating the source of the disease. (Plague) Since the last report was released, this office has received information about the plague in Tongliao, Northeast China. A detailed report is as follows: In early August, several Mongolians contracted bubonic plague and died. Subsequently, 45 Chinese cavalry soldiers in Tongliao also contracted the same disease and died. The Quarantine Office of the Eastern Provinces dispatched personnel to investigate and found the following results: (1) (Xinnailitun) 11 deaths from the disease; (2) (Tuquan) 12 deaths from the disease; (3) (A small village in Kaitong) 6 deaths from the disease; (4) (Kongjiatun) 30 infected cases; (5) (Gaoluosi in Inner Mongolia) 30 infected cases; (6) (Small villages near Tongliao) 1 infected case. The same disease may have occurred in other areas as well, but due to recent floods, it is difficult to conduct a thorough investigation. However, as the weather is getting colder, it is expected that the bubonic plague will gradually decrease. Since the disease is entirely transmitted by rat fleas, and there are now fewer rats, rat fleas will not cause much harm. We recently received a telegram from Fenyang, Shanxi, reporting that plague has also been found in Suide, Shaanxi. According to the most noteworthy information about the plague this year, the regions of Eastern and Western Siberia, which suffered from severe muskrat plague in 1910 and 1920, have not experienced any plague outbreaks this year. It is expected that the ten-year cycle of muskrat plague will be safely passed in 1930 without any outbreaks. This is because the cat-like muskrats produced in that area are very healthy this year. If the muskrats are not infected, they will naturally not transmit the disease to humans."

Severity of Japanese Quarantine 130

When a British ship arrived in Kobe, Japan, a crew member was found to have died from an infectious disease, resulting in the ship being ordered to anchor outside the port for five days before being allowed to enter. Recently, Japanese customs has been strictly inspecting Japanese ships coming from Europe to Shanghai and heading to the Orient. Crew members are not allowed to disembark until they have been inspected for disease and granted permission to go ashore.

The two sandbanks of Dingxing and Ruifeng outside Songkou

Suddenly Submerged by Autumn Tide 131

More Than Ten Men and Women Drowned

The Dingxing and Ruifeng sandbanks outside Wusongkou are located at the mouth of the Yangtze River, making them particularly dangerous during autumn high tides. On the night before last, around 11:30 PM, a sudden gale and tidal surge, combined with rough waves, destroyed the dikes along the coast of the two sandbanks, turning them into a swamp in an instant. Residents were asleep at the time and were awakened from their dreams by the commotion. They climbed onto roofs or trees to temporarily escape. Cries for help were incessant. After about two hours, the tide gradually receded. By daybreak, it was discovered that more than ten men, women, and children had drowned. The bodies were swept away with the receding tide and could not be recovered. Most of the furniture and appliances in the residents' homes were washed away or scattered in disarray. The rice harvested by the farmers was also washed away. The residents of the sandbanks, facing this disaster with no means to recover, presented the incident to the Baoshan County government, requesting that officials be sent to investigate the disaster and that the landowners be immediately notified to provide funds to repair the destroyed dikes to reinforce the embankments and prevent future disasters.

Important News on Yangtze River Shipping 132

2.5 Million Yuan in Cash Transported to Hankou

Hankou needs cash to facilitate business and commerce. The Shanghai banks agreed to purchase foreign exchange and transport it. The British ship company agreed to transport the money in batches each day, a total of 2.5 million yuan, before the lunar Mid-Autumn Festival. In order to ensure safety, the British ship company specially requested the British warship to escort the ships all the way upstream.

Pukou Surcharge: Due to the berthing of military transport ships at the docks of various shipping companies, goods shipped from Shanghai to Pukou are now transferred to barges, resulting in significant costs. Taikoo, Ewo, Nissin, and other shipping companies in Shanghai had already increased the freight rate by 15%. Yesterday, another meeting was held to discuss that the increased freight rate was still not enough to cover the barging costs. It was decided that from October 1st, the freight rate for goods exported from Pukou would be increased by another 15%. The original rate of five taels of silver per ton for general cargo will now be increased to six taels and five mace. The increase has already been notified to various shippers.

New Ship Inaugural Voyage: The Ewo shipping company has built a new ship, "Baohua," in Shanghai, which is dedicated to the Shanghai-Yichang route. The installation of passenger seats has been completed recently. The company has decided that the inaugural voyage to Yichang will be on October 4th. The ship uses a diesel engine and has a very high speed. It is the newest type of fast ship on the Yangtze River. If it travels directly, it can reach Shanghai to Hankou in 24 hours. After this ship starts operating, the "Jianghe" ship will be reassigned to the Hankou-Yichang route and will no longer come to Shanghai.

Cotton Yarn and Cloth: The most important goods for export to the upper Yangtze River are cotton yarn and cloth. As autumn is approaching and the water level of the upper Yangtze River will soon recede, ships over a thousand tons will not be able to navigate to the Sichuan River. Therefore, the Chongqing and Yichang shippers are rushing to export the purchased cotton yarn and cloth. Because in three weeks, the large ships on the Shanghai-Yichang route will not be able to sail. Each day, at least 1,500 to 2,000 pieces of yarn are exported by Jianglun. Of the six companies, Nissin has transported the most. In this month alone, in these twenty days, more than 40,000 pieces have been shipped out. There are still over 10,000 pieces being loaded.

Resumption of Chinese Ships: The number of Chinese merchant ships on the Yangtze River has been gradually increasing since last week. The ships that are currently operating on the Shanghai-Hankou route include "Jiangshun," "Jianghua," "Jiang'an," "Jiangxin," "Jianguo," "Jiangjing," "Ningshao," "Zhaoxing," "Rongxing," "Xin Ningxing," "Longshan," and "Hengshan." On the upper Yangtze River (Yichang route) are "Kuaili," "Hongyuan," and "Hongheng." On the Chongqing route is the "Wuxing" ship. The "Emei" ship of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has also been repaired and will be able to go to Chongqing soon. The ships that have been suspended and will soon resume operations include "Changan" and "Jiangyu." The ships that have not yet resumed operations due to various reasons include "Fulong," "Fengpu," "Changxing," "Jiangtian," and "Dexing."

Regulations on Submitting Documents to the Citizen Training Committee 133

Six Guidelines for Submission Established

Notice Published for Implementation

The Mass Training Committee of the Shanghai Special Municipal Executive Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party hereby notifies all sectors: To inform the public, recently, the people's organizations or individuals in the city often do not follow proper procedures when submitting documents to this Committee, causing inconvenience in the handling of official documents and affecting public affairs. Therefore, the "Guidelines for Submission of Documents by People's Organizations or Individuals" have been formulated and are hereby announced for compliance. This announcement is made on September 27th, the nineteenth year of the Republic of China. The Guidelines for Submission of Documents by People's Organizations or Individuals are as follows: Article 1: All people's organizations or individuals in the city who submit documents to this Mass Training Committee shall follow these Guidelines. Article 2: All submissions from people's organizations in the city must be stamped with the organization's seal, clearly state the address, and be signed by the person responsible. Both the original and a copy must be provided. The paper used for the submission must be in the format recently promulgated by the National Government. Article 3: All submissions from individuals must be signed and sealed by the individual, with detailed information on their place of origin and address. Both the original and a copy must be provided. If it is a complaint, a guarantor's seal must also be affixed. Article 4: When applying for permission to establish an organization or for registration, all forms and documents must be in the format prescribed by this Mass Training Committee. The forms and documents can be obtained from this Committee. Article 5: This Committee will not accept submissions from people's organizations or individuals that do not comply with these Guidelines. Article 6: These Guidelines shall be promulgated and implemented by the Mass Training Committee of the Shanghai Special Municipal Executive Committee.

Notice from the Municipal Organization Department on Changing Party Membership Cards 134

Cards Issued for Two Years Must Be Returned for Replacement

Party Dues and Stamps Must Be Paid in Full

The Organization Department of the Shanghai Special Municipal Executive Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party yesterday issued a notice to all levels of party departments in the city: To inform you about the replacement of party membership cards. If party dues are reduced or exempted after verification, a certificate should be issued by the branch and submitted with the card for review and transfer. This has been previously notified and followed. Now, we have received Notice No. 26 from the Central Organization Department, which states: "Upon inspecting the party membership cards submitted for replacement by various party departments, it was found that some party dues stamps were not affixed in full, and the reasons were not stated, making it impossible to verify. Hereafter, attention should be paid to the following: (1) If the monthly income is less than 20 yuan or if the individual is a student in school, a reduction of 10 cents in monthly party dues is allowed. (2) If the monthly income is less than 10 yuan or if the individual is a farmer, tenant farmer, hired worker, or soldier in the military, a reduction of 3 cents in monthly party dues is allowed. (3) Or if the individual is unemployed or has suffered a major disaster and has been approved for exemption by the district branch to which they belong. In all of these cases, the district branch to which they belong should provide detailed notes on the submitted list, and after verification by the party departments at each level, the list should be submitted to the Headquarters for review. Furthermore, if the date of issuance of the party membership card to a party member is two years or more, they should immediately comply with the Headquarters' Notice No. 19 and submit the card for replacement as soon as possible." This should be followed. In addition to distributing this notice, it is hereby urgently notified that it should be followed. Hereafter, when party membership cards are submitted for replacement, if party dues are reduced or exempted after verification, in addition to the branch issuing a certificate and submitting it with the card, detailed notes should be made on the submitted list for verification and transfer. Furthermore, all branch departments should urge party members whose party membership cards have been issued for two years or more to submit them for replacement as soon as possible. This notice is hereby issued for compliance.

Letter from the Citizens' Association to the Five Directors Regarding the Water Price Increase 135

To: Yuan Ludeng, Yu Qiaqing, Liu Hongsheng, Xu Xinliu, Hu Mengjia, and other five Chinese Directors

Regarding the water price increase:

Dear Sirs, We, the Shanghai Special District Citizens' Federation, are writing to you regarding the recent case of the public concession's water price increase. The Property Owners' Association and the Chinese Ratepayers' Association have repeatedly protested to the Water Company and negotiated with the Public Works Department, sending letters to argue forcefully. However, according to reports, the Public Works Department, at its board meeting held on the 17th of this month, formally approved the 25% water price increase and decided to implement it on October 1st of this year. We are astonished upon reading this. As directors, we did not hear you express any opinions or take any actions at the time. Could it be that you also believe that the water price increase is justified and therefore agreed to it? As renowned figures of this generation, caring for the people as if they were your own children, how can you seek benefits for the citizens and live up to the trust placed in you? Not only that, but regarding the various unfair cases of the Public Works Department treating the Chinese people, you have all remained silent and have not been heard to protest. The citizens' expectations of you have turned from hope to disappointment. Now, let us compare you with the Japanese directors. The Japanese directors occupy only two seats on the Public Works Department board, but they strive to protect the interests of their fellow countrymen in Shanghai. They can be said to be fulfilling their duties to the utmost. Although we occupy five seats, in reality, it is as if we have none. You are ashamed of public opinion and feel guilty in your conscience. How will you explain yourselves? Our Association cannot bear to see you fall into injustice. On behalf of all the citizens, we urge you to do three things: (1) Pay attention to the suffering of the citizens due to unequal treatment and seek to help them. (2) Regarding public construction projects within the concession, you should absolutely protect the interests of the Chinese people and exercise your powers as directors. (3) Regarding the unresolved Chinese cases within the concession, you should be responsible for urging the Public Works Department to resolve them as soon as possible. The above three points are related to the vital interests of the citizens and cannot be ignored for a single day. We hope that you will not be intimidated by the powerful and bear the heavy burden, lest you fail to fulfill your duties and cause many things to go wrong. The citizens have great expectations for you.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Continues to Request Revision of Import Tariff on Cowhides 138

Request to the Ministry of Finance via Telegraph

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing yesterday to continue requesting a revision of the import tariff on red tanned cowhides. The original telegram stated: "The red tanned cowhide industry has requested a revision of the import tariff rules to maintain its operations. In August of this year, we submitted the request and it was approved by you for forwarding to the National Tariff Commission for consideration when revising the new tariff rules in order to maintain the interests of overseas Chinese merchants, etc. It was recorded that the approval was forwarded for notification. The Red Tanned Cowhide Industry Association has now written to state that the Ministry's order to forward the request to the National Tariff Commission for consideration is too remote and uncertain. The increase or decrease in the red tanned cowhide tariff is of utmost importance to the leather industry in Southeast Asia and this city. If the tariff rate is not revised, the Southeast Asian leather factories will not be able to resume operations and the leather industry in this city will continue to suffer losses. Both parties feel pain. At a time when gold is expensive and silver is cheap and all industries are declining, how can the losses caused by red tanned cowhides be further increased? We hope that the esteemed commission will show compassion for the cold market situation and make every effort to maintain it. We again request the Ministry of Finance to approve the revision of the import tariff on red tanned cowhides in the shortest possible time so that the Southeast Asian leather factories and the leather industry in this city can gradually recover their original businesses. We now enclose samples of the goods in accordance with the Ministry's approval and request the customs to review them. We also write again to respectfully request your assistance in providing relief without any delay." Based on this, the red tanned cowhides are produced in Southeast Asia and used in this city. The import tariff rate has not been reduced and the industry is declining rapidly. The request for a prompt revision is a matter of urgency. In accordance with the Association's letter, we continue to request you to review and approve the Association's continued request for a prompt tariff reduction in order to maintain the leather industry. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce respectfully reports.

The Steamships to Chongming Will Not Stop at Two Ports 140

Miaogang and Wugang

All steamship companies in this port operating to Beisha yesterday received instructions from Chongming County stating that in order to comply with the matter, the county government convened a county-wide emergency meeting of various agencies and organizations on the second of this month, at which the district chiefs of the Guanghui Association proposed banning night sailings of steamships to prevent petty criminals from mingling and to maintain security. It was resolved and announced by the county government to prohibit steamship night sailings and to notify various steamship companies and district offices. It was further stated that in view of the current unstable situation and rampant banditry in neighboring areas, the county should strictly implement the resolution for strict prevention measures. In addition to issuing separate notices, the companies are hereby ordered to comply, and all steamships operating to the county, regardless of the port they pass through, are prohibited from entering the area at night. Violators will be investigated and detained by the relevant district office without any delay. This order is of utmost importance. After receiving the order, the companies convened a meeting at the Shanghai Shipping Association to discuss countermeasures. The outcome of the discussion was that Miaogang, Wugang, and other ports under Chongming, steamers leaving from Shanghai to those places will inevitably sail at night. If sailing at day time, it will cause loss both sides and be hard to change. It is a matter of the great responsibility for local security, therefore it has been decided that steamships will temporarily not stop at the two ports under Chongming County to comply with the order.

The Old Case of a Greek Man Killing His Wife Was Retried in Court Yesterday 142

Cases Previously Handled by the Mixed Court

Often Had Two Judgments

The Chinese Official's Judgment Should Be Considered Valid

Legal Issues Will Be Submitted for Interpretation

George C. Poulos, a Greek national residing in Shanghai, murdered his wife, Snow Frieda, on October 13, 1921. He was sentenced to five years in prison by the former Mixed Court. Upon completion of his term, the case was reviewed in court. At that time, there was a consular assessor, who ordered a 14-year imprisonment. Nine years has passed now. Mr. George is now 52 years old. During the summer, it was reported he was severely ill in prison, and the Western prison warden requested the Special District Court to grant him parole. However, after a medical examination, it was deemed that his life was not in imminent danger, and the request was rejected. It is now learned that the Special Court, in order to carry out the review procedures for this case, ordered the police to bring the prisoner to the court yesterday afternoon. Judge Xu Youzhi opened the second courtroom for the trial, and Prosecutor Guo attended to perform his duties. The police lawyer, Ru Bao-yi, requested that George be allowed to sit during the interrogation due to his extreme weakness. The judge granted the request and allowed him to sit after answering. The police lawyer then began his statement, saying that the case was a tragic and premeditated one. A review of the transcripts from the previous trial would make this clear. Two days before the incident, George purchased a sharp knife and lured his wife to a desolate area, where he attempted to stab her. However, the knife slipped from his hand and fell to the ground, foiling the murder attempt. He then changed his plan and strangled his wife to death. There were many witnesses at the time, but due to the passage of time, it is difficult to bring these witnesses to court. If the case had occurred today, the perpetrator would bear a heavier penalty, possibly the death penalty. The agreement on the recovery of the courts, stipulated by the Chinese and foreign commissioners, stated that all judgments made by the former Mixed Court and the Provisional Court should be considered valid. This case was judged by the former Mixed Court, and if the court wishes to deem it invalid and make a more appropriate judgment, the police express their sympathy. It is worth briefly recounting the history of the Mixed Court and the differences between Chinese and Western official judgments. During the winter of 1911, when the revolutionary army launched the uprising and overthrew the Qing Dynasty, the Chinese officials of the Mixed Court left their posts, and the court was left without a leader. The consular body then stepped in to take over, and consuls from various countries took turns hearing civil and criminal cases involving Chinese and foreigners in the concession. The consuls and the Chinese officials hired by the Municipal Council were paid by the Municipal Council, and the Chinese officials were not appointed by the Chinese government. Therefore, they were also subject to the direction and supervision of the Municipal Council. The power of judgment was entirely in the hands of the consuls, and the Chinese officials' position was equivalent to that of advisors. The Chinese officials' judgments in criminal cases were limited to five years. It is unknown why this limitation was put in place. The current Mixed Court in the French Concession still follows this practice. For example, if an offender needs to be sentenced to more than five years, they are sent to the Chinese authorities in the Chinese area for handling. However, since the consular body took over the court, it has not allowed the transfer of cases involving sentences of more than five years to the Chinese authorities, and the Chinese officials of the court have this verdict of "reviewing the case in court upon completion of the five-year term" to remedy the situation. Therefore, if the judge believes that the term of the sentence handed down by the Chinese officials of the former Mixed Court has expired, the offender can be released, and the police will not object. However, if the judge believes that the previous judgment was too lenient and that a retrial is necessary to increase the sentence, that would be even more appropriate. There are still about 200 prisoners in Western prisons who are in the same situation as in this case (i.e., the Chinese and Western judgments are different). Most of the crimes they committed were serious robbery and kidnapping. The sentences handed down by the consuls were all more than 10 years, while the Chinese officials still made the judgment of "revisiting in court after serving the five-year sentence." Therefore, if the defendant in this case is released today, all 200 or so people should also be released. Conversely, all of them must be retried. However, if all these 200 people are released, it will inevitably create security problems, and even a slight move will affect the whole situation. Therefore, it is important to be cautious from the beginning. Therefore, the lawyer requests that the judge submit this case to the Supreme Court for interpretation, and the police will comply with the instructions after receiving the Supreme Court's interpretation. Judge Xu then declared that the court's motion was based on Article 4 of the annex to the agreement. However, the "judgment of the former judicial organ" mentioned in the agreement refers to the judgment made by the judges who constituted the judicial organ. Even if the consul attending the court was involved in the trial of the case in fact, he cannot be regarded as a judge. Therefore, if the judicial organ has two judgments in the same case, naturally only the judgment of the judge, i.e., the Chinese official, is valid, because the consul does not have the authority to adjudicate. The motion for review is not to release all defendants who have been imprisoned for more than five years. Serious cases that are severely punished by the court should be handled according to the law and are not subject to any restrictions. The lawyer's request to request an interpretation of the legal issues will be forwarded to the court after a written opinion is submitted. Then, the defendant was questioned about the facts of the case. The defendant only answered a few words before his old illness recurred and his body trembled. The judge felt that he was seriously ill and ordered him to be returned to custody and adjourned the court.

The Kidnapping Case of Xu Anhou Was Pronounced Yesterday 143

Nine Bandits Each Imprisoned for Five Years and Deported

And Sent to the Inland Court for Trial

Xu Anhou, an employee of the Shanghai Bank residing at No. 41 Brainee-Montauban Road in the French Concession, hired a car at 8 a.m. on the 2nd of last month, intending to go to work at the bank, but he was kidnapped by bandits and hidden in the Fanjiatai area on the border of Qingpu in western Shanghai. The perpetrators then demanded a ransom of 300,000 yuan from the victim's family, but the ransom was not paid. Paul, a Western detective of the special agency of the French police; Jin Jiulin, a detective inspector; Li Yaolong, a chief detective; Qian Yumin, Mao Jingen, Wang Rusong, Lu Zhulin, Bao Ziying, Zhou Bu-guang, and other plainclothes detectives learned of the situation and, along with other plainclothes detectives on duty, rushed to the bandit den in Fanjiatai, where they apprehended nine bandits, including Zhang Peiqing, Zhu Sannan, Chen Debao, Zhou Jinsheng, Luo Xiaohai, Xi Xiangsheng, Qin Pangen, Wang Shuji, Chu Yunlong, and others. They shot and killed one bandit, Zhang Amao, on the spot, seized three handguns, and rescued the hostage. The details have been reported previously. Yesterday morning, the police summoned the victim to bring the defendants to the French Court for investigation. The Chinese and Western officials presided over the criminal court and investigated the case. A person named Jia acted on behalf of the plaintiff and described the circumstances of the kidnapping. Then, Sacier, the Western chief detective, described the process of cracking the case and submitted the confession of the handgun. Judge Zhu Chengshen read the confessions of the various bandits submitted by the police one by one. When asked, the bandits all admitted to the crime without hesitation. The Chinese and Western officials then sentenced Zhang Peiqing, Zhu Sannan, Chen Debao, Zhou Jinsheng, Luo Xiaohai, Qin Pangen, Ding Shuji, and Chu Yunlong to five years in the Western prison and deportation, and the handguns were confiscated.

The Water and Land Police of Daan Port Outside Wusong Port Vigorously Suppressed Pirates 144

Daan Port in Haimen County, located outside of Wusong Port, is located on the coast with many estuaries and harbors, making it easy for pirates to come and go. It was previously occupied by a large group of pirates who suddenly abandoned it, and then returned again. The Fourth District and Eighteenth Squad of the Wusong Water Police repelled the bandits, as repeatedly reported in this newspaper. However, the day before yesterday, more than 500 pirates suddenly arrived again on more than 30 pirate ships and landed on the port. The pirates were all equipped with rifles, as well as Mauser pistols and handheld machine guns, resembling a military force with great momentum. Wu Yaochun, the magistrate of Haimen County, immediately joined forces with Lin Cha, the captain of the Eighteenth Squad of the Water Police, and Zhong Jun, the leader of the First Platoon of the Eighteenth Squad of the Water Police, and Cheng Rusong, the captain of the County Police Brigade. At about 10:00 p.m. that night, they attacked the pirates head-on by land and water. The two sides engaged in a fierce battle for about three hours. The pirates stubbornly resisted with their numbers, acting in an extremely ferocious manner. Fortunately, Captain Lin and Platoon Leader Zhong bravely launched fierce attacks by land and water, continuously firing rapid-fire cannons. The pirates were unable to withstand the attacks and began to flee to the pirate ships and set sail south. The water and land police took advantage of the victory to pursue the pirates, and many pirates were shot and fell into the water. In this battle, more than a dozen firearms were seized, and five members of the water and land police were injured. They have been sent to the hospital for treatment. There are currently no traces of bandits in the area, and the residents are celebrating. Magistrate Wu of Haimen has submitted a request to the provincial authorities to commend Captain Lin, Platoon Leader Zhong, and Captain Chen of the County Police Brigade for their effective defense.

Full Text of the Judgment in the Kaiming Publishing House Case 146

The case of World Book Company suing Kaiming Bookstore, which was judged by Judge Cheng Shangfeng of the Shanghai Special District Court, sentenced Du Haisheng, the manager of Kaiming, to a fine of 30 yuan for public insult. The details have been reported in the newspapers. Now, we have found the full text of the judgment and copied it below: (Main text) Du Haisheng is fined 30 yuan for the crime of publicly insulting others. Zhang Xichen is not guilty. (Facts) The self-plaintiff, Shen Zhifang's World Book Company, published a book this year which the defendant, Du Haisheng, manager of Kaiming Bookstore claimed was copied. The content of the Standard English Reader was quite similar to the English reader published by Kaiming Bookstore in the past. After the defendant entrusted a lawyer to negotiate, Lin Handa, the editor of World Book Company, came forward to discuss, but no agreement was reached. Then, Kaiming Bookstore published various terms such as the World Book Company's Standard English Reader being copied from Kaiming's English Reader in various newspapers in Shanghai from August 26 to 29, and printed small pamphlets and distributed them everywhere. The self-plaintiffs and others believed that the defendants had harmed their reputation and credit and violated Articles 325, Paragraph 2, 330, and 328 of the Criminal Law, and successively sued the court. (Reasons) The Standard English Reader published by World Book Company has two poems that are the same as the English Reader published by Kaiming Bookstore, and the source was not indicated. Therefore, Du Haisheng's dissemination of defamatory words against World Book Company is not comparable to fabricating facts. According to its circumstances, it is nothing more than self-defense of its rights, according to Article 326 and Article 327, item 1, of the Criminal Law, it is not punishable. Although the disseminated words are beyond the scope, there is still a basis and it is not comparable to rumors. It is also difficult to constitute the crime of harming credit under Article 330 of the Criminal Law. However, the Shenbao newspaper published on August 30 and the pamphlets distributed by the defendant contained "I hope that more knowledgeable people will be hired to edit books in the future and be careful in doing things." It also cited two sections of "World Strange Tales," Ai Zi stayed at an inn and lost his fox fur, which was obtained from a traveler's luggage. One section is compared to theft, and the other is no different from pointing out that the other party's editors are all ignorant. This kind of blatant and insulting words deliberately exceed the necessary scope of their statement and make people feel embarrassed. It should constitute the crime of insult under Article 324 of the Criminal Law. Except for the defendant Zhang Xichen, who is only an ordinary clerk and should be exempted from discussion, it should be judged separately according to Article 315 of the Criminal Procedure Law as in the main text. If you do not accept the decision, you may appeal to the collegial panel of this court within 10 days from the day after receiving the judgment.

The Case of a Monk Sodomizing a Disciple Opens 151

The monk Miao Wang was accused of sodomizing Zheng Hehou, a pastry shop apprentice, at No. 70 Tangfang Lane on the 25th of last month in the lunar calendar, causing inflammation of the anus. Chen Ali, the shop owner, reported the incident to the police and had Miao Wang arrested and brought to the District Court. After examination and interrogation, the prosecutor filed a public prosecution citing the crime of disrupting public morals. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhao Yongzhou opened the third courtroom for trial. The defendant, Miao Wang, claimed to be 24 years old, from Anhui Province, and currently registered at the Haichao Temple in Lujiabang as a monk. "I am innocent because they know that I came from Mount Putuo, and they intended to extort 20 yuan from me. At 2 p.m. on the 25th, Zheng Hehou came to me at the second floor of Lao Er's house at No. 70 Tangfang Lane to ask for money for steamed buns, but I didn't owe him any money, so I hit him and he cried. There was no one else in the room at that time. Later, Lao Er came home and the child had not yet left. He beat me because I was making trouble upstairs. I am a monk and don't do such things." Chen Ali claimed to be 31 years old, from Nengzhou, and ran a pastry shop at No. 56 Tangfang Lane. "Zheng Hehou is an apprentice, only 13 years old, and has only been here for more than a month. Page 16

To ask for money, later the child cried because I was not far away, I thought he was being beaten, so I went to argue, and Lao Er was beating Miao Wang severely, because the matter was explained, the child fought casually and instead advised him, unexpectedly the child shouted butt eye pain, I asked him why, he said he was sodomized by the monk, so I knew, so I wanted Lao Er to hand over the man, when he was sent here it had been examined and it was true, and the child's excretion has blood." Zheng Hehou claimed to be 13 years old, from Tongzhou. "I don't know the monk. I went to his house to ask for money, about 1,600 yuan. The monk was in the back building. Impersonating Someone to Defraud Goods Was Discovered on the Spot 152

At 9:00 a.m. the day before yesterday, two people from Ningbo, Dai Qin-gen and Jin Cai-yuan, went to Jinchangxiang Hardware Store near Broadway Road with a note from Moli-Pound Company to collect paint worth more than 200 yuan. Moli then sent a colleague with Dai to the warehouse to pick up the goods. Upon closer inspection, the Moli stamp on the note was different from the previous stamp. When asked about this, Moli realized that it was a forgery. Fortunately, the goods had not been picked up, so he reported it to the Hongkou police, who sent detectives to arrest Dai and Jin. Yesterday, they were sent to the Special District Court, where Judge Feng interrogated them. According to plainclothes detective Shen Dehui, the defendant had not only once defrauded goods by using other people's names. He requested an extension to allow for further investigation. When questioned, Dai confessed that Jin had given him the note and told him to pick up the goods. Jin first escaped at the entrance of Jinchangxiang and was later arrested by him in the Chinese Park. He was in fact deceived by him, he said. Jin confessed that he had worked for Moli before, but had no way to make a living after he resigned. Therefore, he asked a fortune-teller to write this note and forge the stamp, and entrusted Dai to pick up the goods from the store. The court ordered the two defendants to be detained and rescheduled for questioning.

Autopsy of Three Prisoners Who Died of Illness 154

Three prisoners in the Western Prison of Tilanqiao died of illness the day before yesterday. One was Chen Agui, who was sentenced to four years in prison by the former Provisional Court on June 24 of last year for the crime of intimidation and fraud. Another was Li Changming, who was also sentenced to five years in prison on September 18 of the year before last for the crime of intimidation and fraud. They both suffered from lung disease, which led to their deaths. Their similar crimes and illnesses led to their deaths and were to be pitied for each other. Another person named Yuan Dekui was sentenced to three years in prison for the crime of abducting children. His illness had become increasingly severe, and his medication was ineffective. He died the day before yesterday. The three bodies were all taken to the autopsy center on Feilun Road yesterday morning by Prosecutor Guo of the Special District Court to be identified one by one. Chen Zhangshi, the wife of Chen Agui, signed a statement to collect his body for burial. The other two bodies had no relatives, so the Pushan Villa claimed the bodies for burial.

A Record of a Cruel Teacher Abusing His Apprentice 155

Zhao Sangen's Life Is Over

Neighbors Express Great Dissatisfaction

Mo Xianggan, a 27-year-old silversmith from Shaoxing, resides at No. 1, Alley 88, Yujia Lane, Xiaonanmen, Southern City. His wife is notoriously shrewish, and the neighbors are wary of her. However, Mo's character is even more cruel. In the spring of this year, someone introduced a fellow villager named Zhao to be his apprentice. The boy's name is Sangen, and he is 13 years old. Since arriving at Mo's house, Mo and his wife have treated him as a master and mistress and abused the apprentice in many ways. Every day, they force him to get up and work at dawn, and if he is not careful, he is scolded by the mistress. He is not allowed to rest from morning to night, and if he is lazy, he is dragged to the kitchen, stripped of his clothes by Mo, and severely beaten. Or they would use huge wooden sticks and iron tools to whip him, and he was forbidden to cry out. After the beating, he was told to put on his clothes and continue working as usual, without being given any food. Every time he was punished, he was denied food. For several months, the apprentice had been covered in wounds, with broken skin and blood flowing. However, he did not rest from his work, but only lamented and shed tears in secret. The neighbors in the area had long been accustomed to this. On the 21st of this month, the neighbors caught a glimpse of a thick hemp rope around the apprentice's neck. At first, they did not know its purpose, but later they learned that if the apprentice was slow in his work, Mo would pull the rope tightly from behind, making it difficult for him to breathe. At this point, the apprentice could not shout, but could only tremble his hands and feet. After a long time, he was allowed to loosen his private punishment, and then he adjusted his breathing and continued to work. When the neighbors realized this, they felt that his cruel actions were too inhumane and tried to persuade him, but they were scolded and dared to rely on his rudeness, saying, "My apprentice should be supervised. It's none of your business. If I beat him to death, I will of course be responsible for compensation. What's the big deal?" The neighbors were unwilling to do more. Unexpectedly, at about 9 a.m. yesterday, the apprentice suddenly died. Mo then quietly bought a coffin and prepared for the funeral. Who knew that the nearby neighbors Zhao Gensheng, Zhou Nanrong, Dong Rongxiang, Dong Rongsheng, Wu Fugao, Wu Shangkui, etc., had learned that the apprentice had died from injuries caused by the teacher's abuse. Therefore, they could not contain their public anger and jointly submitted a petition to the relevant first district and third precinct, requesting a thorough investigation. The precinct chief Jin, according to the previous reports, believed that his abuse of the apprentice was so cruel and rare that he should be severely punished. He immediately sent patrolman Zhao Shuyan to the location and found that the deceased Zhao Sengen's neck and feet were swollen and covered in scars. He arrested the murderer Mo Xianggan and brought him back to the precinct. Precinct Chief Jin ordered that the case be transferred to the Shanghai District Court for interrogation, and ordered Zhu Runqing, the head of the 19th shop, to report to the court for an autopsy.

Minutes of the Standing Committee of the Chinese Leprosy Society Women's Association 159

The Women's Auxiliary of the China Leprosy Relief Association held its first standing committee meeting of the term at the residence of Mrs. Xiao Zhiji on Gordon Road yesterday (the 25th) at 4:30 PM. Dozens of female leaders such as Mrs. Yan Fuqing, Mrs. Zhang Jiafu, and Mrs. Xi Boshou were present. Dr. Bolton then gave a speech, saying, "The lepers in Nanchang mostly make a living by begging. They are now being detained by the municipal government in dilapidated houses in the west of the city, where their lives are even more difficult. Fortunately, with the assistance of the China Leprosy Relief Association, a new-style leprosarium is being built and is expected to be completed next month." Pastor Shi briefly stated, "The original site of the dilapidated leprosarium in Hainan has now been rebuilt into a magnificent municipal government building. Enthusiastic local people have repeatedly proposed to move the lepers to the Daqin Leprosarium in eastern Guangdong, but due to various reasons, it has never been realized. Now, it is planned to build a new hospital on the spot, which has been supported by the local government and the Chamber of Commerce, and with the cooperation of the China Leprosy Relief Association, it can be realized soon." Next, the officers for this term were elected. The results were as follows: President: Mrs. Zhang Jiafu; Vice President: Mrs. Xiao Zhiji; Secretary: Ms. Cai Jingxiong; Treasurer: Ms. Yan Feiwen. By the time the meeting adjourned, the city was lit up.

Inability to Marry Leads to a Robbery 160

Ruyizi Cries Out "Robber!"

Li Xianggui Detained by the Authorities

Li Xianggui, a 22-year-old man from Yangzhou, lives at No. 5 Yude Lane, Lannidu, Pudong, and works in a bathhouse tea room. On March 16th of the lunar calendar this year, he was betrothed to Ruyizi, the daughter of Xu Xia, a woman from Gaoyou who lives in a shack behind the Huatong Stack, with Wang Shaofu, a foreman from the Taikoo Dock, and Ding Shen, an old woman from Yangzhou, as matchmakers. Ruyizi is 18 years old and works in the Rihua Cotton Mill in Lujiazui. At that time, it was agreed that the gift-giving ceremony would be held on the sixth day of this month. However, Xia's mother is stubborn and clinging to old customs, demanding a large sum of money and all kinds of gifts, claiming that if they are not provided, it will be difficult to agree to the marriage. Xianggui's monthly income is limited, and upon hearing this news, he was inevitably panicked. He repeatedly asked the matchmakers to intercede with the woman's family, requesting a reasonable reduction. Although he was tired of talking, Xia's mother remained unmoved. Seeing that the date for the gift-giving ceremony was imminent, and he would be unable to cope, it was bound to become a laughingstock. Out of desperation, he discussed with his brother Xianglin and decided to abduct the bride. First, they would abduct Ruyizi and take her home, then they would negotiate with her family. If the other party still insisted on the original agreement, then what's done is done, and the other party would probably have no way to object. Once the plan was decided, on the evening of the day before yesterday, at five o'clock, he gathered many relatives and friends and waited near the factory next to the British-American Tobacco Company. Before long, Ruyizi arrived gracefully. Xianggui was afraid of grabbing the wrong person and causing a scandal, so he carefully examined her to make sure it was her. Then he personally stepped forward, hugged Ruyizi around the waist, and ran quickly towards the Pudong Bund, hoping to take her to the home of a relative or friend in Puxi for temporary shelter. Unexpectedly, things did not go as planned. Ruyizi did not recognize the person hugging her as her fiancé, so she shouted "Robber!" A nearby patrol officer heard the noise, chased after them, stopped Xianggui, and arrested Xianggui's brother Xianglin, who was helping him, as well as Zhang Asi from Yangzhou and Li Gan, a woman from Yangzhou. They took Ruyizi along with them to the fourth team of the police station and transferred them to the third district. District Chief Zhang took the group into custody for preliminary interrogation and summoned Ruyizi's mother, Xu Xia, and the original matchmakers, Wang Shaofu and Ding Shen, to the case for questioning. According to the defendant Xianggui's statement, the woman's family demanded excessive gifts, which he was unable to provide, so he had no choice but to resort to this measure. Moreover, Ruyizi had gone through proper betrothal procedures and would be his wife sooner or later, so he asked for forgiveness. According to Ruyizi's statement, the matter was entirely decided by her mother, and she had never been involved. According to the statements of the three people who helped with the abduction, they admitted to helping Xianggui abduct the bride. According to Xu Xia's statement, the defendant forced her into this freely, and she requested that he be investigated according to the law. According to the two matchmakers, the woman's family demanded a large sum of money, which was true, but they had promised to find a way to raise 50 yuan to lend to the defendant. They were completely unaware of this sudden abduction. The district chief verified the statements and considered that bride abduction was an evil custom inherited from the Qing Dynasty. In this era of innovation, such a forced custom should no longer exist. He immediately ordered that Xianggui and the other three be charged with obstructing local customs and reported to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. The original matchmakers were released on bail, and the plaintiff was advised that if they wished to prosecute the defendant, they could file a lawsuit in the local court in accordance with the law.

Renowned Physician Treats Typhoid Fever 164

Recently, many cases of hidden heatstroke have been discovered in this city. This is because in the summer, people are exposed to heatstroke, and in the early autumn, they are attacked by sudden cold, so both latent evil and external cold occur at the same time. Initially, there are symptoms of fever, chills, headache, and aching joints. If not treated properly, the fever will increase, the tongue will become dry, and the lips will be parched, or dangerous signs such as white spots will appear, which is commonly known as typhoid fever. Tao Gengyu, a physician at the Dunren Public Institute in Sunjia Lane, Zhonghua Road, outside the Great East Gate in this city, has been practicing medicine for many years and has rich experience. He is also confident in treating this disease, so patients who go to him for treatment are always cured.

Tianchan Stage to Cease Performances at the End of the Month 167

Resolution of the Public Works Department Board Meeting

The Da Mei Evening News reported that the issue of the operating period of the Tianchan Stage has been under negotiation for a long time. According to the Public Works Department's plan, the building is considered to be extremely dangerous in case of fire and must cease performances or be relocated by the end of this month. The manager of the stage previously stated that the artists all had contracts and that the losses would be immeasurable if performances were stopped. He repeatedly appealed to be allowed to continue performances until the end of the year, arguing that the building would not be dangerous within this year. The Chinese directors also interceded on his behalf. Recently, at a meeting of the Public Works Department Board, based on the opinion of the department's legal counsel, it was considered that the situation would be very serious in the event of a fire at the stage, and the head of the Engineering Department also believed that, from a safety standpoint, it could not be considered a first-class building in the event of a fire. Therefore, a director suggested that the manager be ordered to stop performances before the end of this month. After a brief discussion, it was decided to order the head of the Engineering Department to negotiate with the manager of the stage to stop performances before the end of this month, and the Fire Department staff was charged with taking special fire prevention measures. The chairman of the department, Fei Xindun, also believed that if safety was the main concern, then other details were not important and not worth considering.

Citywide Labor Union Petitions for Permanent Existence 169

States Old Customs of Improper Dismissal Still in Use

Huadong News Agency reported that the city's labor unions, due to the central government's temporary suspension of the abolition of labor unions and the government's approval of the continued use of old customs for dismissing workers, have successively received instructions from the municipal and central authorities for approval and have considered them to be insightful and have indicated their adoption. However, the citywide labor unions still listed the reasons why labor unions should exist permanently, demanding that the central government determine the organization and promulgate an explicit text, stating that the old customs of improper dismissal should be abolished quickly, and dispatched five group representatives and seven representatives to Beijing the day before yesterday with official documents to petition the Central Executive Committee, the Central Training Department, the National Government Executive Yuan, the Legislative Yuan, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, the International Labor Bureau, and the Labor Director of the eight organizations. The following are excerpts from the two petitions: (1) Petition for approval to determine the permanent organization of labor unions and to separately formulate single regulations for the organization of shop employees to ensure protection and national transportation matters. Upon investigation, the recently promulgated Law of Industrial and Commercial Trade Associations by the Central Government is based on the reason that to develop commerce, labor-capital cooperation must be realized first, and to realize labor-capital cooperation, workers must join the trade association before they can melt into one furnace and jointly seek the development of business. The central government has made painstaking efforts to maintain national commerce and eliminate the prejudices of labor and capital. For the sake of their own interests and for the future of commercial and labor transportation, they have no choice but to express their concerns. I dare to express the advantages and disadvantages to the superiors. According to the absolute freedom of the people to assemble and form associations, all those who earn a price with physical or mental strength to maintain their lives are workers, and the teachings of the Prime Minister should be regarded as the criterion. The organization of labor unions is in line with the doctrine and is relevant to the needs of the times and the environment. Moreover, labor unions have never been behind others in the history of the revolution. Workers and merchants belong to the same people and the same banner, and both workers and merchants can organize groups. Why is the labor union alone not allowed? Even if shop employees over the age of fifteen can send representatives to participate in the trade association, what will happen to shop employees under the age of fifteen? Moreover, it is still a question whether the representatives they send can implement their proposals in the trade association. Judging from the daily relationship between labor and capital, it is undoubtedly that the workers' representatives will be suppressed by the capitalists' representatives. In this way, the workers' representatives will have only a nominal title and no actual power. It is unnecessary to say that unfortunately, workers feel that their position is not guaranteed, are confused by the heresies of reaction, and take risks that endanger Anning. Is it not even more serious that the affiliated associations want the implementation of laws and regulations to be in line with the doctrine and in line with the needs of the times? As the main body, the affiliated associations aim to realize labor-capital cooperation and develop commerce as the premise, only because capitalists have too deep feudal concepts, so they use revolutionary means to promote their reflection. Chu Zhu has never had a single doubt. Although the paths are different, the destination is the same. If the organization of labor unions is abolished, tens of thousands of workers will be at a loss and not know where to go. The advantages and disadvantages are clear to the affiliated associations. Regarding this case, although we have submitted a request to the Shanghai Municipal Training Association to forward it to your department, we have been approved to temporarily suspend the cancellation in accordance with the previous instructions. However, the two words "temporary suspension" make the affiliated associations feel anxious. If we can't avoid it, we can only send Wang Yongchang, Chen Shuzhi, Huang Shaoxu, Hu Shouqi, Zhu Xiaoyun, Sang Yutang, and Zhao Zhenhui, editors of the Shanghai Business Press Distribution Labor Union, the General Affairs Section Labor Union, the Calligraphy and Stationery Fan Labor Union, the Silk and Cloth Dyeing Labor Union, and the Pharmaceutical Industry Labor Union, as seven representatives from five groups to visit the superiors and plead for your consideration of the people's sentiments and approval of the labor union organization, and to separately formulate single regulations regarding the organization of shop employees to comply with, so that shop employees can have appropriate guarantees. From now on, labor and capital will each have a basis, and the party will guide and the government will supervise, so there will be no actions outside the orbit that will endanger commercial development and social peace. I hereby present it. The way to hire and dismiss shop employees according to old habits does not conform to laws and regulations and does not conform to public opinion. Please order its revocation. Hu City Social Bureau Announcement No. 106 stipulates that the hiring and dismissal of shop employees shall be temporarily handled in accordance with the old habits of each industry, and on August 26, the local newspapers published news about the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce's investigation of the dismissal habits of various industries. The affiliated associations are terrified and cannot express their feelings. We believe that the government has long had clear provisions to abolish old habits. In the past, the Party and government jointly announced during each lunar calendar festival to prohibit the use of old habits and not to dismiss employees without reason. An Ji then created a self-contradictory policy, and it is even more unreasonable to use old habits when promoting the national calendar. Moreover, the labor unions of Shanghai City have been legally organized and have signed labor-capital contracts with capitalists. The dismissal methods are detailed in the articles, and both parties should absolutely abide by them. If a piece of paper from the Social Bureau causes the contracts of mutual trust and adherence between labor and capital in each industry to be completely destroyed, it will not only fail to eliminate the disputes between labor and capital, but will also increase the disputes. Moreover, a thorough investigation of the causes of labor-capital disputes in the past is nothing more than inequality in treatment and unjustified dismissal. The reason why capitalists have not dared to openly abuse coercion recently is because there are labor-capital contracts. Once the old habits are restored and shop employees are freely hired and dismissed, the affiliated associations dare to predict that not only will enthusiastic revolutionary movement and hard-working labor movement shop employees be discarded, and the statistics of social unemployment will inevitably increase, but labor unrest will also be inevitable. The impact on social peace is not small. Combining the above points, it is undeniable that Announcement No. 146 of the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau does not conform to laws and regulations and does not conform to public opinion. For the sake of social peace and to protect the on-the-job employees from unemployment, the affiliated associations are responsible and cannot bear to guarantee the wives of the shop employees, and even more cannot bear the government's laws and regulations to be like children's play. Therefore, we dare to send Wang Yongliang, Chen Shuzhi, and Huang Shaoxu, the head of the Shanghai Business Press's Distribution and Editing General Affairs Labor Union, Hu Shouqi of the Calligraphy and Stationery Industry Labor Union, Zhu Xiaoyun of the Silk and Cloth Dyeing Labor Union, Sang Yutang of the Pharmaceutical Industry Labor Union, and Zhao Zhenhui, etc., as seven representatives to rush forward and petition, hoping that they will consider the hidden worries, comply with public opinion, and approve the order to revoke. I am extremely eager to wait for orders. Shanghai Business Press's Distribution Office Labor Union, Shanghai Pharmaceutical Industry Labor Union, Shanghai Calligraphy and Stationery Industry Labor Union, Shanghai Silk and Cloth Dyeing Labor Union, Shanghai Pharmaceutical Industry Labor Union, Shanghai Sauce Industry Labor Union, Shanghai Pawn Industry Labor Union, Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Cloth Industry Labor Union, Shanghai Pudong Electrical Labor Union, Shanghai Longan Grocery Labor Union, Shanghai China Merchants Bureau's Five Wharves Labor Union, Shanghai Miscellaneous Grains and Oil Cake Exchange Labor Union, Shanghai Wine Industry Labor Union, Shanghai Su Ning Tea and Food Labor Union, Shanghai Cigarette Exchange Labor Union, Shanghai China Food Company Labor Union, Shanghai Porcelain Industry Labor Union, Shanghai Tea Industry Labor Union, Shanghai Business Press's Editorial Office Labor Union, Shanghai No. 1 Chinese Public Bus Labor Union, Shanghai Huiguan Labor Union, Shanghai South Goods Labor Union, Shanghai Parasol Labor Union, Shanghai Pollen Labor Union, Shanghai China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Labor Union, Shanghai Business Press's General Affairs Office Labor Union, Shanghai Water and Electricity Industry Labor Union, Shanghai Incense Industry Labor Union.

Another Dispute Occurred Yesterday Morning

The situation yesterday is published as follows:

Another dispute occurred yesterday morning. At about 8:00 yesterday morning, a large number of workers, about 200, gathered in the area of the French Water and Electricity Plant in Lujiazui, demanding work. These people were all new workers from the previous strike period. The situation was very serious for a while, and the company authorities did not respond. An Open Letter to All Sectors of Society The labor union yesterday issued an open letter to the labor community of the city, saying, "Fellow workers of the city, before the previous labor movement, the capitalist of French imperialism used destructive and destructive means to break our group organization. They used several unscrupulous people in our labor union to instigate all our fellow workers.
