Fortunately, their conspiracy was heard by a loyal comrade who still had a conscience, so they reported to the public, and their tricks were finally exposed and did not become a reality. However, the capitalists of French imperialism could not implement their planned plan because these labor thieves could not implement their planned plan. Money and spirit inevitably suffered a major blow. However, their destructive work was also unyielding. Later, when we wanted the capitalists to improve their treatment due to environmental pressures and life pressures, the capitalists took advantage of this opportunity and wanted to fundamentally eradicate our labor union, so they resolutely rejected our legitimate demands. Although we wanted to use the expression of a slowdown to make them realize, they had already honestly and rudely used the deportation policy to close the iron gate and not allow us to work. This method was obviously to cut off our lives. On the one hand, they also used the club labor thieves of the Transportation Department to destroy our tightly knit labor movement. Fortunately, we were tightly knit and were not moved by it. At the same time, we also received the assistance of our fellow workers in the city, and finally won the labor unrest on the surface. However, after investigating the actual situation, the capitalists have not fully fulfilled the conditions signed, and the oppression and abuse have become more and more intensified. However, our fellow workers are still enduring it, and sometimes they only negotiate with those responsible for mediation. How did they know that the French imperialists had bought off the thugs in the club this time and wanted to assassinate us, and they also destroyed our legitimate and legal worker group's association, and even insulted the Prime Minister's portrait. How can this be tolerated? In total, the French imperialists have repeatedly tried to destroy us in the past, which was still relatively secret. Now, it has become more and more obvious. All the fellow workers of this association, in addition to reporting the details to the higher-level authorities for investigation, have to report the beginning and end of this incident to my city's fellow workers. At the same time, I hope that my city's fellow workers will provide as much assistance as possible to save us from the fire and water."

The Team Leader Meeting Was Held Again Yesterday. Yu Haiquan Was Publicly Elected as Chairman. He Reported on the Purpose of the Meeting, Briefly Stating that Foreigners Had Instructed New Workers to Conflict with Workers in the Factory Today. Fortunately, the Police Arrived After Hearing the News and Drove the Others Away. Then It Was Resolved that the Capitalists Would Add Ten New Workers. Only After the Capitalists Fulfilled the Various Conditions Proposed by the Labor Union Within the Limited Time Could They Agree. Otherwise, the Labor Union Would Notify the New Workers to Leave the Factory When Necessary.

Hengfeng Yarn Factory Workers Strike 171

The Municipal Training Committee Rejects Approval

According to the National News Agency, workers at the Hengfeng Yarn Factory, due to the factory's long-standing harsh treatment, low wages, and excessive fines, launched a sudden strike on the 24th of this month when wages were distributed and significant deductions were made for fines. They formed a strike committee and presented eleven demands. Simultaneously, they reported the strike's progress and demands to the Municipal Training Committee, seeking assistance. Upon receiving the report, the Municipal Training Committee, noting that the factory had no labor union, that the demands had not been reviewed and approved by the Party, and that the strike had been initiated without following legal procedures, deemed it illegal and potentially disruptive. Besides thorough investigation, yesterday, the Committee issued a formal reply to all workers of the factory: “Your report states that the employer refused your demands, leading to a factory-wide strike, and requests swift assistance. Upon investigation, the factory lacks a labor union, and the proposed labor-management terms were neither submitted to this Committee for prior approval nor to the Social Bureau for mediation following the event, before the unauthorized strike, which is highly inappropriate. You are ordered to immediately resume work; your request is denied. This is the order.”

Departmental Approval Requested for Maintaining the Livelihood of Diviners and Astrologers 172

Yesterday, Cai Boqin, a representative of Shanghai’s diviners and astrologers, received approval from the Ministry of Interior, document number 125, which stated: “The original petitioner, Cai Boqin, a representative of Shanghai's diviners and astrologers, etc., submitted a document stating that their professions are being banned, their livelihoods cut off, and detailing the difficulties of changing professions. They request a temporary suspension of the ban before a suitable solution is devised, to allow them to maintain their livelihoods. Having reviewed the submission, instruct a letter to be sent to the Shanghai Municipal Government to devise appropriate measures according to Item 3 of the 'Measures for Abolishing Divination, Astrology, Witchcraft, Shamanism, and Geomancy' promulgated by this Ministry. This is the approval."

Wu Qishu Passes Away 173

Mr. Wu Linshu, since falling ill last month, has been ill for a month. Despite being treated by renowned doctors, he did not recover and passed away at 2:00 PM yesterday at the age of 52. Mr. Wu was from Wu County, Jiangsu Province, and had resided in Shanghai for a long time. He engaged in numerous business ventures, possessed profound knowledge, and demonstrated a magnanimous demeanor, tirelessly supporting and promoting younger generations. When officials sought to entrust him with important positions, he politely declined, as his ambition lay in developing industries to benefit the people's livelihood. He was particularly attentive to the textile industry, and the Tongyi Yarn Factory and Yida Yarn Company that he managed achieved remarkable results. He served as a director of the Shanghai Branch of the Bank of China, the Commercial Press, Ewo Yarns, Shanghai Yarn Factory, Chongxin Yarn Factory, Minsheng Yarn Factory, and Ningbo Hefeng Yarn Factory. He was also the chairman of the Shanghai Tongyi Yarn Factory, the China Cement Company, and the China Industrial Promotion Bank. Additionally, he served as the vice chairman of the Shanghai Chinese Yarn and Cloth Exchange. He resigned from his position only a year ago due to heavy workload. After the establishment of the National Government, government authorities issued two-fifths of customs duty treasury bills and specifically ordered Image of the Late Wu Linshu

the formation of the Two-Fifths National Treasury Bill Custody Committee. Mr. Wu was appointed by the authorities as a standing committee member. Mr. Wu often believed that the decline of China’s textile industry was due half to capital shortage and half to a lack of scientific management within textile factories. Therefore, in 1928, he traveled to Europe and the United States with his close friend Hu Jun’an and his son Ruiyuan to investigate textile management and cotton seed improvement. They spent a year in the cotton-producing regions of India, England, France, Italy, Germany, and the United States, conducting research. Upon his return, he contributed his findings to China's textile industry. Consequently, many in the textile industry directly or indirectly benefited from his guidance and achieved effective management. Mr. Wu was also extremely benevolent and over the years, he donated a considerable amount of his earnings to domestic and international charitable causes, as well as funding for schools and hospitals. It is reported that the funeral will be held on the 29th, and a memorial service will be held at a later date. Upon hearing of his passing, people from all walks of life expressed profound grief.

Free Talk

A Laughing Matter 177

— Seafarer

Butcher: Madam, why haven't you come to buy our meat for so long?

Female customer: Last time I bought a piece of your beef, it was so tough it could have been used for the sole of a shoe.

Butcher: Then why didn’t you just make a shoe sole out of it?

Female customer: It was so tough, even nails couldn’t go through it.

Affable lady (speaking to her friend's young daughter at a dinner party): Good child, you are only seven years old, and you can already help your mother?

Young daughter: Yes, every time we have guests, after they leave, my mother always asks me to help her check if any silver spoons and ivory chopsticks have been stolen by you.

A: Your son always takes a car to the office every day. Why do you always take a rickshaw yourself?

B: Because he has a rich father, but I, unfortunately, do not.

Diner: Waiter, why is your pork chop so tough?

Waiter: Sir, why don't you use a knife to cut it off?

Diner: I have already cut off a small piece, but it is still impossible to chew in my mouth.

Waiter: Since the knife can cut it off, it is certainly not tough. You should blame your own teeth, not us.

Anecdotes of Tan Yankai 178

— Sun Choucheng

Tan Yankai, Premier of the Executive Yuan and Acting Chairman of the National Government, passed away at 9:55 AM on the 22nd of this month due to cerebral hemorrhage at his private residence in the capital. The National Government ordered all institutions in and out of Beijing to fly flags at half-mast for three days from the date of receiving the telegram, and to suspend all entertainment and banquets to express mourning. The facts have been noted in this newspaper, and now I will write about some trivial matters of his life as a memorial.

Tan's Beijing residence is located on Chengxian Street, not far from the National Government. It is a Western-style building facing the road and is not very magnificent. It is said to be rented from someone else. There is a guard at the door to provide security. The gatehouse is unusually small, with only one gatekeeper. Sometimes, he is busy receiving and sending letters and telegrams, and if one wants to convey information, he is flustered and unable to cope, unable to take care of everything. The reception room is downstairs, and the facilities are very simple, with only a large dining table and a dozen chairs. The four walls have neither ornate mirror frames nor paintings and calligraphy by famous people. Ordinary guests are led into this hall by the gatekeeper. Outside the hall, there is a staircase leading to Tan's study. Ordinary guests are not allowed to enter the courtyard at will. There is a little space decorated with flowers and evergreens. Tan has a large appetite and also likes to drink, comparable to Li Bai and crabs. He is kind-hearted, and he always helps his impoverished fellow villagers who come to him for loans. He treats people with kindness and never speaks harshly. Recalling last spring in Beijing, I and Ma Xiaojun, the chief of the General Staff, and Su Minsheng, the chairman of the General Chamber of Commerce, visited him at the same time on official business. Because there were so many documents and guests at the National Government, we could not talk in detail. He made an appointment to meet us at his private residence the next day. At 9:00 AM, we took a car to the reception room. It was already full of distinguished guests. After handing in our name cards and sitting for a while, the servant led us to the study upstairs for a tea talk. The study was small, with only a desk, a coffee table, two armchairs, and a bookshelf. Famous paintings and calligraphy and ancient musical instruments were hung on the wall. The bright windows and clean tables made it feel very refined. On the desk was a copy of the History of the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom, which was a manuscript with very elaborate characters. It is said that there were many historical materials about the Hong Yang Rebellion. At that time, due to the strict prohibition of the Qing Dynasty, the descendants of private authors feared the disaster of words and privately destroyed them. Now, he planned to collect them from various sources for reference and editing. When we were leaving, he accompanied us to the downstairs very warmly. A month later, I was drinking with a friend in the Fanghu wine shop in Shanghai's Xiangfen Lane. Tan also came upstairs with a friend for a drink, wearing a cloth robe and not bringing any followers. Those who did not know him would not know that he was an important figure in the National Government. During the chat, he inquired in detail about the rise and fall of Shanghai's business, which showed that he cared about people's livelihood. Unexpectedly, this farewell was the last time we would meet. Seeing his posthumous image in the newspaper yesterday, I couldn't help but feel emotional. I have supplemented the above record to express my admiration and to show that I will never forget him.

A Rice Joke 179

— Qiushui

A friend said that a certain county in Jiangbei has always suffered from rice shortages. One day, a new county magistrate, whose surname was Mi (rice), took office. The people saw that he was well-educated and had the qualities of a scholar, so they thought of making things difficult for him. They gathered at the county office to describe the rice shortage and asked the new county magistrate to find a way to solve it. The county magistrate was afraid that the crowd would cause trouble, so he stood up in public and said hastily, "Although my surname is Mi, I did not bring any rice. If you need rice, please ask the rice shops, do not ask me." His words were originally humorous, but he had no intention of causing trouble. Unexpectedly, the clever people led a team to rob the rice shops in the city. When the police tried to stop them, they said, "We are here on the order of the county magistrate." Thus, trouble arose. When the matter was reported to the superior, the superior knew that the words came from the county magistrate and that there was no excuse for his crime, so he issued an order to investigate him. The county magistrate Mi lost his official position because of his surname Mi. The matter is also interesting. I have written it down to show that the ancients' warning about being careful with words has its origins.

The Swallow Tower in the Swallow's Nest 180

— Wang Meiqu

I have been sick for a dozen days since the beginning of autumn and have not been able to leave the West Building of Meiyuan. Last Wednesday, the Green-Clad Lady (i.e., my close friend Wu Liuyi) came to say goodbye before going to the capital. I told her about the boredom of living in the building. The Green-Clad Lady said, "Pan Pan did not leave the Swallow Tower for ten years, how can you not bear it for a dozen days?" We smiled at each other and ended the conversation. On September 21, I went to the residence of my friend Tong Runan to relieve my boredom. Runan is hospitable and all the guests were famous scholars. We were sipping tea, chatting, and commenting on calligraphy, painting, bronzes, and inscriptions. Suddenly, a young girl with pigtails jumped in and shouted, "Fourth Aunt is here!" Then I saw an aging woman without makeup but still charming, slowly entering the door, nodding and smiling to the guests, looking familiar. Runan's wife told Meiqu, "This is an old friend of Runan, and now she nests in the Swallow's Nest." Meiqu has seen so many women who have fallen from grace in Shanghai that he is not surprised. He is only surprised that Runan, a famous scholar, appreciates someone outside the realm of female beauty. A guest named Woyouzi understood my meaning and smiled at me, saying, "Where is there no talent? What a narrow view!" Then, while the woman was chatting with Runan, he told me about the woman's background. Meiqu said, "Strange, the Swallow's Nest has such a person, surpassing the Swallow Tower." The woman was one of Shanghai's famous beauties in her youth, and Runan was also among her admirers, but he had no intention of marrying her. When spring deepened, she chose to marry someone. The man had a little talent and a sharp pen and could help people settle lawsuits. He was a lawyer before the time of modern lawyers. The woman and the man were very happy together. After only a few years, the man went blind and could no longer wield his pen. The family became increasingly poor. The woman did not change her mind because he was blind and continued to support her mother-in-law and manage the household. The blind man had been relying on others to eat in bed for fifteen or sixteen years. Some old friends hinted to the woman, saying, "I love him to the end. Although his eyes are blind, his heart is not. He loves me as before. If I abandon him, his mother and son will both end up in the gutter." So she ran the Swallow's Nest and used all her earnings to support her mother-in-law and son. Runan valued her character and also helped her as much as he could. Guan Panpan was able to maintain her chastity because Zhang Jianfeng was willing to let her, and now she is immortal. But the woman entrusted to her is very humble, and there is no Jianfeng's illustrious reputation that can be used to achieve fame. She has sworn to remain chaste. If she had ordinary skills, she would not seek to live in the Swallow's Nest. It can be said that she is worthy of comparison with the Swallow Tower. The fact that Runan's adopted daughter calls her Fourth Aunt is because she has always been known as the fourth oldest. Her real name is unknown.

A Record of Daoist Zheng's 按導 Techniques 181

— Ma Yincai

Mr. Yuan, Daoist Zheng of Fang County, is famous for his skill in 按導 (pressing and guiding). Those who have been cured by him are too numerous to count. As far as I know, the niece of Mr. Zhou Junliangcai, the secretary of this city's municipal government, was eight years old when she contracted a severe swelling disease. Western and Chinese doctors all believed that the disease was in the kidney. Daoist Zheng alone believed that the disease was in the stomach and intestines. After treatment, yellow water leaked out of the pores of her legs, her urination was smooth, and she also passed a lot of black feces and white phlegm. Her illness was as if it had disappeared. Also, this summer, Mr. Cen Chunxuan of Guangxi suddenly became unable to move, with symptoms similar to stroke. He was introduced by his brother, Mr. Xilin (who had suffered from a serious illness and had been cured by Daoist Zheng), to seek Daoist Zheng's treatment. After one 按導 session, he could move. After three more 按導 sessions, he recovered. Also, Mr. Feng Mujun of Ningbo suffered from stomach problems for more than forty days in the summer and autumn. The pain became increasingly severe over time and he could not sit up. Daoist Zheng believed that the disease was caused by the depletion of heart qi, which led to damage to the spleen. If not treated quickly, it would become even more difficult. After six or seven 按導 sessions, he recovered. Mr. Feng told me that once 按撫 (pressing and stroking) was applied to his chest and stomach, he felt hot air rushing down to his dantian, steaming and bubbling, directly reaching his coccyx. When 按導 was applied to his bladder, the hot air traveled from his thighs to his knees, leisurely reaching his heels. This was the most amazing and refreshing sign. Daoist Zheng's 按導 method involves circulating the qi throughout the body and gathering it in the palm of the hand, directly transferring it to the patient's body. This is why it is so effective. Daoist Zheng can also take the pulse of the abdomen to predict life and death. He is especially good at treating critical and severe illnesses, such as bleeding, dysentery, abdominal pain, soreness in the hands and feet, severe liver, stomach, and heart qi pain, as well as typhoid fever, damp heat, and all kinds of difficult and complicated diseases. No matter how dangerous and critical, he can respond effectively. It is completely different from the current popular intangible massage and manipulation techniques. His disciples have compiled Daoist Zheng's Medical Efficacy Records, and Mr. Chen San'yuan, Mr. Wang Xicun, Mr. Cheng Zida, and Mr. Zhu Qiangcun all have inscriptions. These gentlemen have all benefited from his medical treatment. He is truly an outstanding physician.

Miscellaneous Records of the Great Calamity in Changsha (Part 1) 182

— Litian

The Shanghai newspapers have published many facts about the looting and arson caused by the Communist bandits' intrusion into Changsha. However, there are still many situations that not only people from other provinces do not know, but also the people who have experienced it may not necessarily know. Because they were in that kind of red terror and were busy fleeing for their lives, people did not have the leisure to ask about these endless, tragic things. Now that the unprecedented tragedy has passed, it is still worthwhile to write down a few of the things I saw and heard at the time to provide the people living in the concessions with something to talk about "after tea and dinner."

As soon as the Communist bandits entered the city, they set fire to it and posted slogans and notices, asking "the people of Changsha to work hard to participate in the riot." After this "deterrent," they demanded 700,000 yuan in cash from the Chamber of Commerce, and euphemistically called it "donations to support the revolution." Their notice stated, "The riots will seize Changsha to relieve the suffering of the proletariat and abolish all exorbitant taxes." But the Chamber of Commerce received this extortion order, which said that those who did not pay would be beheaded. They immediately convened a meeting of the defense corps. In addition to requiring the major merchants to raise a portion, all citizens, regardless of their poverty, were required to donate two months of rent. As a result, some of the people who could not afford to pay committed suicide, and some were sent to the "Red Army Headquarters," because those who did not pay were "counter-revolutionaries."

At the same time, the Chamber of Commerce used this condition of paying money to ask the Red Army Headquarters to find a way to "maintain order in the provincial capital," because the general riffraff and hooligans took the opportunity to rob, and with the addition of a decree rewarding those who reported on others, they were even more fierce. At that time, the commander-in-chief of the Red Army generously issued a notice stating, "Those who are hooligans and rob for no reason will be beheaded." Therefore, the way of looting shops was different. First, the Red Army or the spear team entered the shop to search and loot, and then sent armed or spear-wielding hooligans to guard the door. The Red bandits gathered outside the door. After the Red bandits looted the good goods, they shouted loudly when they left, "People, come and share the wealth!" Then these intangible Red bandits swarmed in and carried out a second search. Sometimes the Red bandits destroyed the shops and even tied up the bosses and their wives, torturing them to force them to hand over cash. Although most of the shopkeepers ran away, many were caught. At this time, the Red bandits were not "selective in their prey." As long as they opened a small shop, they were "奸商" (treacherous merchants). Their slogan was only "Farmers, Workers, Soldiers!" Merchants and intellectuals were among those who were overthrown.

A Record of Attending the North-South Chess Match 183

— Sent from Hong Kong

The long-planned North-South Chinese chess competition began on August 11th after the arrival in Hong Kong of Zhou Deyu and Lin Yixian, two masters from North China. This competition was organized by the South China Chinese Chess Research Association, which was founded last autumn by members of the Confucian Society. Chess masters from all walks of life responded enthusiastically. Since its establishment, the association has been brewing the idea of a North-South chess match. Last winter, a human chess competition was held at the South China Athletic Association's stadium. The initial plan was to have players from both North and South China participate, but the North China players were unable to come, so players from Guangzhou and Hong Kong filled the ranks. Only now has the North-South chess match become a reality.

The competition venue was the hall of the Chinese YMCA, with seating for over 500 people. Tickets were priced at 20 cents each, and a season pass for all nights was sold for one dollar. However, there were only about 300 spectators each night. This is because not many people are fond of this game, and it is difficult to make those who are not interested sit still for several hours. The competition was scheduled to start at 7:30 PM. I arrived on time on the first night and found that many spectators had already arrived. On the stage hung a chess board of about eight feet in length and width. The chess pieces were about four or five inches in diameter, making them quite clear to see from a distance. Next to the large chess board was a small table for the players to use their ordinary chess boards for the game. Each time a piece was moved, the referee loudly announced it, and two other people followed by moving the pieces on the large chess board for the audience to see. The order was quite good.

The South China players were Li Qingquan and Feng Jingru, both over 40 years old. Li's head was already half bald. Both had been immersed in Chinese chess for twenty or thirty years. They had reached the point of perfect mastery, as the saying goes. Li's style of play was steady and cautious, never taking risks. However, his defense was strong and he rarely made mistakes. Feng's original name was Zejiu, and he enjoyed the reputation of "Chess King." His style of play was erratic and unpredictable, sometimes taking risks to attack the enemy, with only a step separating him from being killed. Therefore, the audience often held their breath. However, Feng rarely failed in his risky attacks. The title of Chess King was truly not undeserved. In addition, there was Huang Songxuan, whose skill was also on par with Feng and Li, and they were known as the three wonders of the South China chess world.

In the first night's match, the top player from North China, Zhou Deyu, took the field. Zhou was a first-class player in the North China chess world, having traveled across several provinces without meeting an opponent. South China sent Li Qingquan to meet him. It was guessed that the intention was to use Li's steady style to maintain a draw, even if he could not win, in order to avoid losing the first match and ruining his reputation. Zhou had a handsome appearance and gentle demeanor, and was only in his thirties.

At 7:30 PM, a Mr. So-and-so, the announcer, announced the reasons for the meeting. When explaining the reasons for promoting Chinese chess, he quoted extensively from classical texts, proving himself worthy of being a member of the Confucian Society. His tone and attitude during the speech fully expressed the air of a scholar. The speech lasted about ten minutes, and the audience was quite impatient, eagerly awaiting the start of the great battle. When Li and Zhou were introduced to the audience, they applauded loudly.

In the first game, both sides moved very cautiously, with few surprising moves. At 9:15 PM, Li of South China drew with Zhou of North China, with a single chariot, cannon, pawn, and all elephants and advisors against Zhou's single chariot, horse, pawn, and all elephants and advisors. In the second game, the brilliant moves of both sides gradually emerged. Zhou was particularly lively. After thirty or so moves, Zhou had lost his horse and Li had lost his cannon. Zhou then sacrificed his chariot to try to kill the enemy. The audience initially looked surprised, but then understood the intention and applauded repeatedly. At this time, Li was in a precarious situation, but managed to save himself by defending well, sacrificing his chariot to remove Zhou's central cannon and reverse the dangerous situation. He then used the advantage of a full set of elephants and advisors, a cannon, two horses, and a pawn against Zhou's single chariot, pawn, and all elephants and advisors. At this time, Zhou's defensive skills were also greatly demonstrated, using his chariot to disperse the opponent's horses and cannons. Although Li sacrificed a pawn to remove Zhou's two advisors, his horse was ultimately trapped and unable to move. The whole game had to end in a draw. By this time it was already 11:30 PM. The scheduled three games to determine the winner were postponed to another day.

That night, in addition to ordinary spectators, almost all of the South China chess masters, such as Huang Songxuan, Deng Tieru, the champion of the Hong Kong Open Chinese Chess Competition, Zeng Zhanhong, Liu Shoupeng, Chen Depai, Duo Ruisheng, and Huang Zhangji, gathered. Huang Songxuan and Deng Tieru even placed chess pieces next to their seats and commented on the merits and demerits of Zhou and Li's moves. Zeng Zhanhong, the chairman of the North-South Chinese Chess Competition, carefully recorded Zhou and Li's moves with a pencil. Feng Jingru, who was not scheduled to compete that night, sat in the audience and commented on the moves of both sides in a low voice with his friends, gesticulating vividly. At the same time, Li Qingquan on the stage remained calm and focused on the chess board from beginning to end, without ever looking away. Zhou, on the other hand, was relaxed and often shifted his gaze to look at the audience after each move. From this, one could see the depth of his skill.

The Reason for the Apparent Looseness and Secret Tightness of Silver Funds 188

Credit funds released cannot be returned as scheduled

Several businesses went bankrupt due to lack of cash flow

Recently, the appearance of silver funds has been quite calm, but the actual content is extremely tense. The general phenomenon of silver shortage has made it very difficult to draw in and purchase bills. According to people in the industry, the reason for the apparent looseness and secret tightness is that in the past week, credit transactions and outstanding funds released by money shops have repeatedly failed to be repaid as scheduled, and several businesses have been forced to go bankrupt, owing tens of thousands of dollars in shop funds. With so many bad debts accumulating, money shops are naturally greatly affected. Those who are affluent and have sufficient bills will inevitably choose the best and carefully screen and select, and will not relax. This has caused a great relationship in the market atmosphere. Fortunately, money shops now hold a cautious and contractionist doctrine for lending, so they are not as large as before. Even if there are accumulated debts, the amount must be limited or there is no danger of affecting the overall situation.

The Current Month's Wheat Futures Plunge More Than One Qian 197

Yesterday, wheat futures went down across the board. The current month was the last trading month, and the bulls, due to frequent shortages of spot wheat, a sluggish flour market, and the pressure from foreign flour and wheat, had no intention of taking delivery and aimed to close out their positions. They sold off in the market in batches. Seeing the bulls' offers, the bears watched and bought in. Therefore, although the opening price in the morning was still between 4 liang 7 qian and 3 to 4 fen, it steadily declined afterward. The closing price was squeezed down to 4 liang 6 qian and 3 fen, down more than 1 qian and 1 fen. This kind of squeeze on bulls nearing the delivery date is also rare. However, after this transaction, the number of deliveries this month will be very few. Far-term months declined as well, due to the lower flour prices, the lack of spot wheat transactions, and the impact of the sharp decline in the near term. The closing price was down 1 qian and 1 fen for the current month, and 7 fen for the October, November, January, and February terms. The December term was down 6 fen.

Shanghai telegrams were not forwarded. Only Yongxing imported five bales of Jin Sangye brand top-grade 13-15 denier raw silk at a price of over 980 taels, and the market was generally silent.

High-Grade Zhenmei Green Tea from Gaozhuang Continues to Sell Well in Europe 200

Yesterday, Gaozhuang Zhenmei green tea from Wuyuan and Tunxi and other regions continued to be imported by Baochang, Yongxing, and other firms. Transactions were still active. Among them, top-grade early-spring teas were offered at 225 taels. However, ordinary Zhenmei tea remained sluggish. Large merchants from various regions were still selling off in small quantities. Needle-shaped and fine-leaved teas also continued to be traded, but selling prices were generally trending downward.

Yarn and Cloth: Eastern Goods Experience the Most Significant Price Increases 201

Qingdao and Tianjin Still Actively Searching, Sichuan and Hubei Also Active

The local cotton cloth market remained stable. Yesterday, there was a slight improvement in actual sales, with the local market being the most active. Over 200 pieces of 11-pound coarse cloth and over 100 pieces of 13-pound coarse cloth were traded, all wholesaled to inland areas. Fifty pieces of 18-pound "Sky" brand Niuzhuang Yingkou cloth were handled at a price of 8 liang and 7.5 fen. Fine twill was in short supply. Due to active searches by inland merchants, there is a high probability of continued price increases. The market for undyed fine cloth has been stagnant since sales declined, and it has remained quiet. As the end of September approaches, the market is becoming increasingly stagnant and stable. The Tianjin group handled over 100 pieces of coarse twill yesterday, and prices showed a slight increase.

Eastern goods continued to rise yesterday. Both Qingdao and Tianjin merchants were still actively searching for goods, and Sichuan and Hankou merchants were also highly active, resulting in a situation of supply not meeting demand. Fine serge rose by another 2.5 to 5 li. Lakeside Pavilion Joy has been sold at 2 qian and 9 fen. Zijin Mountain Baizi also requires 2 qian and 8.5 fen. Sales of wool-silk cloth are also active. San Matou cloth is priced at 2 liang and 2.5 qian, and the available stock is already limited. San goods have reached the same price. Straight tribute woolen cloth and satin are in short supply, and prices are high, leading to a temporary boom.

Miscellaneous News: The Shanghai North-South Money Shops will be closed for one day on October 1st. The Gold Exchange will also be closed on that day. All cash public bonds for the October term will be resolved on the 2nd, as announced to the market yesterday. Also, due to the Mid-Autumn Festival in the Lunar Calendar (October 6th), all banks have pre-agreed to close for one day as usual, and the Gold Exchange will also be closed. Business will resume as usual on the 7th.

Shanghai Market News The Yulun Silk and Satin Bureau on the east side of Wangping Street, Nanjing Road, announces that the bureau's official opening grand sale for one month is coming to an end. Recently, customers have been extremely crowded. All newly arrived autumn clothing materials are also sold at low prices. In addition to price cuts, high-quality real silk handkerchiefs are also given as gifts. It is said that goods are especially cheaper on Sundays. The Meida Silk and Satin Foreign Goods Company on Fourth Malu Road announces that the company specializes in various silk and satin goods and has long been famous in society. Since holding a large auction with full-length fabrics plus 20-30%, the business has been booming for the past 20-30 days, and business is extremely prosperous, it is said. The Ford Motor Company announces that Mr. McCarthy, the manager of the company in Danhua Wharf, has invented a new method to prove the economy of using Ford cars. Mr. McCarthy said that people who want to buy cars often consider the value of the car and the cost of maintaining the car. Such people must not want to waste money. I first took a savings box from the bank and tied it to the front of the car’s splash board with the silver slot facing upwards. This place is in front of the driver and within sight of the buyer. When driving for one mile, I stopped and took one cent from my purse and put it into the savings box. The car buyer did not pay attention to it. Then, every two or three miles, I put a cent in as before, and when the car traveled five miles, I put two cents into the savings box again. At this time, the car buyer felt very strange. Finally, I told the car buyer that this is the money saved by using a Ford car, and explained the calculation method in detail, and thus obtained the purchase of the car, it is said. Lao Jinlong Foreign Company announces that the White Orchid perfume managed by the company is a French product, fragrant and rich, with a lasting fragrance. It has the fragrance of a king and has the effect of refreshing the mind. The price is low and the quality is good. It is the best in the market of fragrant products. Major foreign grocery stores and major pharmacies all sell it, it is said. Gongli Socks Factory announces that the factory has specially set up a retail and wholesale department on Nanjing Road Hongmiao to meet the needs of customers. The student brand silk stockings issued are cheap and of good quality. During the opening period, there are special discounts. There are also more than a thousand kinds of cosmetics for sale, all produced by famous German factories, it is said. Theater News The World Grand Theater at the corner of Qingyun Road, Zhabei, announces that since the beginning of autumn, every time it has screened top-quality famous films, the seats have been full. The glamorous and sensual love film "Circus Woman" of the Dahua Lily Company will be shown at the theater starting today (27th). The film stars Zhou Wenzhu and Zhang Wenqing, with mysterious and sensual performances, exciting plots, and wonderful photography that can fascinate the audience, it is said. Paris Grand Theater announces that from today, the Monte Carlo Dance Troupe, which is famous all over the world, will be invited to perform amazing skills and moving songs and dances. The troupe has a large number of talents and superb skills. It is welcomed everywhere when performing in various countries. The theater, in order to satisfy the eyes and ears of the people of Shanghai, spent a lot of effort to hire it to come to Shanghai to perform, and also screened the hilarious detective film "Who is the Murderer" starring the king of comedy, Raymond Griffith. The laughter is rich and can be called a masterpiece, it is said. Fudan Film Company announces that the company's "Twenty-Four Knights of the Jianghu" has released four episodes, and since its release, it has been praised by all parties. Now the fifth episode is about to be completed. The heroine of this episode is Ms. Hu Shan, whose reputation is comparable to that of her sister Hu Die, and she is especially good at performing martial arts dramas. This time, Mr. Yu Boyan has repeatedly suggested directing, and the results are very impressive. Other aspects such as the greatness of the scenery, the exquisiteness of the costumes, and the twists and turns of the plot are all enough to make the audience pleasing to the eye. When it is released, I hope everyone will not miss it, it is said. Youlian Film Company announces that the company's well-known "Wild River Heroine" film is now, at the request of all parties, allowed to combine the first two episodes, a total of 20 large volumes, at the Central Grand Theater for three days starting from the 30th of this month. From October 3rd, the latest released third episode will be screened immediately. In this film, "Breaking the Beauty Pagoda" is still starred by Ms. Xu Qinfang, and the emotions are becoming more and more tense, full of enthusiastic and exciting impressions. The fourth episode "Battle of Wansonglin" and the fifth episode "Double Breaking of White Ox Mountain" have also been filmed and will be released soon, it is said. Medical News The Huichun Hospital founded by Dr. Zhou Zhaonan, who studied in Japan, announces that the hospital has moved from Haining Road to Zhejiang Road opposite the Xianshi Company last month. Dr. Zhou specializes in pediatrics, stomach diseases, pulmonary tuberculosis, venereal diseases, and all kinds of surgical operations. The gynecology department is handled by his wife, female doctor Chen Huiai, it is said.

Youth Corner Impressions of a Trip to the North Su Ling (VI) A City of Snow Gray skies are like the face of a widow covered in black veil. The pale blue, hazy sun is like the bewildered eyes of a virgin. The cold wind patrols, and snowflakes scatter sparsely, ah. The city trembles. The high heels of women dance on the slippery sidewalks. The beards of men with beards and their high leather collars are frosted. I mingle alone in the crowd, my heart and legs trembling. I have always been someone who likes to live in the city. In Shanghai, although I was unemployed for years and struggled daily in poverty, I never left Shanghai. It wasn't because I dreamed of making a big development or a big plan in Shanghai. I didn't want to leave city life because a mysterious, trembling force lurking in the city seduced me. But I was willing to be tempted and led by it. In the metropolis, there are complex and different kinds of "appearances," and the center of the metropolis is so chaotic and conflicting. So we live in it as if we are sitting in the middle of a symphony being played. Perhaps some people will laugh at me for having an empty pocket, or even a hungry stomach, and still wanting to walk alone on such a fleshy, material street. Yes, but how do they know that my spiritual gain is greater than my physical gain? Before going north, I was worried that I would not be able to live a city life after coming north. But what I feel now is that this snowy city has a strange taste. That is, I can't see the desert and the black forest that I wanted to see, but I don't lose anything. I sit on the chairs for people to rest on beside the sidewalk in front of the big department store windows, watching the night gradually fall. The sky changed from gray to black. The lights came on. Sparse snowflakes still fell, glittering like white flower petals under the streetlights. The music of the dance halls and cafes sounded, and this sound trembled in the snowy night. The number of pedestrians on the street increased at night, but I was very surprised that this was not a concession or a foreign country. Why couldn't I see Chinese people around me? Indeed, the broad minds of the Chinese people are admirable. The Chinese people also generously give land to these large numbers of stateless White Russians to live on. Look, isn't Harbin entirely a White Russian country? Most of those big stores are run by them. The ignorant Chinese people mutter "Ah, Lao Maozi" when they see White Russians and are afraid of them. Yes, aren't the Red Russians who constantly shoot at China with machine guns and cannons at the border born the same as these White Russians? Confused thoughts invaded my brain. I drank half a glass of vodka in a small food shop to dispel my thoughts and warm my cold body. So I drunkenly crossed the wide street, turned into a dark alley, and went home to comfort Mi Luo. Today is Sunday morning, and Zeng brother came to see me. The autumn wind seemed to have already blown from the sea, once blowing the thin blanket on my lonely couch, making me wake up in the middle of the night with cold. But in the past day or two, it has grown its fierce flames again, clearly displaying the power of a tiger. The pavilion faces east, and the sun shines early in the morning. Who can bear to sit here in boredom? I went out with Brother Tang and walked north on Sichuan Road. After wandering on the street for a while, I bought a newspaper and casually flipped through it, walking to the front of the Shanghai Grand Theater, arousing the interest in watching a movie. "Walking around aimlessly is too boring and hot. Let's watch a two-cent movie. No matter what it shows." "Okay, my treat. Two cents is very cheap. Maybe there is philosophy besides the movie for you to study, brother," Zeng said with a smile, his long hair waving. Walking inside, it didn't take long for the scenes to start playing before the audience. Because there was a lot of slapstick, there were bursts of laughter, but the story seemed very mediocre. I still remember a point in the whole thing: "There was an old woman who relied on her daughter's favor with the mistress and lived with her daughter, able to enjoy some leisure. However, there was one thing that she always felt very sad about, that is, her husband had been missing for a long time, making her stare at his photo in a daze day and night. Sometimes she would even crazily mistake passersby. She tried her best to ask people to inquire everywhere, but she could not get any real news. Later, her daughter fell in love with someone, and the lover was a capable inventor who gave the old woman a lot of comfort in all pleasures, but she missed her husband all the more. Until her last death, she still shouted wildly that she wanted to find her husband." It was almost twelve o'clock when the movie ended. Zeng and I squeezed out of the crowd. Our eyes, which had been in the dark for two hours, could not open when we saw the sun. It seemed that Zeng's face looked a little strange, but I didn't pay attention to it. Walking to the intersection of Bazi Road, we took a tram back. As soon as we sat down, he said to me sadly, "I'm going to get a haircut this afternoon and want to take a photo."

Page 26

"What's the use?" "Mother wants to see me. I haven't been back for four years." His voice was sad. "It's really inconvenient to travel back and forth to your distant hometown." "Yesterday I received a express letter saying that my mother is seriously ill and wants to see a photo of me, her beloved son, whom she hasn't seen for four years." I secretly looked at Zeng. I didn't dare to say anything more, and there were no suitable words to comfort him. I could only remain silent, letting the tram creak forward in the wind. It wasn't until after dinner that Zeng said he had something to do and left. In the evening, I wrote a letter to comfort him. "Brother Zeng, I expected that you would be plunged into complete sorrow today. Indeed, it is such a heartbreaking thing for a wandering son to be away from home and for a loving mother to be waiting anxiously at the door. Moreover, she is old, sick, and in danger, with only the hope of seeing a photo of her beloved son whom she hasn't seen for four years. We have known each other for two years, and we have only shared the same sorrows. We have had heart-to-heart talks late at night and have given me long poems in return. Especially after reading the original manuscript of your entire 'Sister's Remains,' I have gained a great understanding. You, the poet, have sung of the colors of sorrow: 'On a face with unexpressed sorrow, countless haggard lines have been added, symbolizing decline, disease, old age, and death.' 'Weak shoulders deeply bear the heavy cross of the past five years, traveling in the desolate desert with melancholy.' 'Beautiful youth plays a hazy and indistinguishable funeral music, eliminating the bitterness of life. The sorrowful and mournful dirge sends my surging and endless heart's blood, spurting out endless tears.' 'Now I am separated from my beloved hometown and sinking into the abyss of a foreign land.' Indeed, you have completely and nakedly exposed all the sorrows of a poet. However, I can understand that you are definitely not moaning without illness. There is an unspeakable pain in this, and I am afraid that only those who suffer from the same disease can appreciate it. Recently, the banner of national literature and art has been grandly displayed, and you have undoubtedly rushed to the front line of the Chinese literary world and bravely become a pioneer. Your great poems have suddenly taken a new direction, abandoning the praise of the bright moon and the clear breeze and singing the glory of our Chinese nation. This clearly shows that you have grasped the correct thinking and have begun to embark on a great future. Four years away from home is nothing. The responsibility in the future is even greater. If your loving mother knows that you are improving and working hard, she will surely smile when she sees your thin face, even if an unfortunate event occurs. At the same time, look at me, alone and unable to pursue the joy of parents and the laughter of siblings in the white poplar woods. How can I not be sad? However, I have realized that sadness is futile. I have no ill-gotten wealth to offer to your old mother, nor any vain glory to comfort your old mother. Everything is in the journey of wandering, relying on a surge of life's hot blood and working hard. Only an upward and unremitting heart can fly back to your hometown from afar and lie in your old mother's thoughts. I will give you your articles again: 'This unfortunate life, this desolate and helpless surroundings, was not it already destined on the fate stone pillars of the previous two centuries? Joy needs to be pursued with courage, and happiness needs to be seized with effort. Historical facts tell me this, and I feel it.' 'The past has become an elusive illusion, and the future may contain a glimmer of bright hope. From now on, I can only gather my inherent energy and move forward to fight against the darkness that prevents the free progress of mankind and seize the national glory shining in front of the times.' We need to move forward, and young people need guidance to improve. Here, I can pray that your old mother has recovered her health. As long as you work hard." White Hair Chun Originally, who can eternally grasp the enjoyment of happy youth and escape the arrival of the image of old age? The giant wheel of time is turning ruthlessly. Will it allow anyone's request and slow down its urging? Can the flourishing of plants and trees in spring be exempt from the withering of autumn? This is the decision of natural conditions and also the creation of natural conditions. Then, isn't the growth of my white hair ordinary and ordinary again? But I feel that the decision of natural conditions is ultimately natural. It is not a standardless scale, and I have surpassed this standard. I believe that people of my age should not have white hair, but like my actions, I cannot escape this sign. Oh, this white hair that indicates the extinguishing and fading of my youth, this white hair. In fact, it is not something to be sad about, and in reality, I will not be sad about the discovery of white hair. What I think about is the changes in life in this year. Although the changes in life in this year are not painful or traumatic, they are worth eternally commemorating and eternally commemorating. I don't know how, at dawn today, when I was still hazy, Brother Zhi suddenly discovered a precious thing and pulled my hand and said, "You have white hair." "Do I have white hair?" I asked doubtfully. "Yes, and there are several." "Then can you pluck them out for me?" Brother Zhi agreed and lay down on the bed to pluck them out for me. After plucking for a long time, one root came out. At that time, I looked at it for a long time and couldn't say anything for a while. Finally, I trembled and forced a smiling face and said like a prayer, "This is a white hair worth commemorating, oh, white hair. I want to keep it." "………………………" However, what about Brother Zhi? He also has a lot of white hair. What does this represent for him? For years, I don't know why I started to get involved in the world. So my heart has also changed since then. I understand very well that my age is too childish, but when I repeatedly think that "childish age is a rice bucket," I feel at ease. I only ask myself to strive. As for what the results are, then it can be said that it has made me know a little more about the world and at the same time has made me spend my youth. Standing South Sun Photography I remember Brother Zhi saying unintentionally one night that my youth was coming to an end, but I hadn't enjoyed anything in my youth. Naturally, I had nothing to say to him and only asked in response, "How do you know that my youth is coming to an end?" Brother Zhi couldn't help but feel very sentimental and said, "You are the same as me. I was drawn into the vortex of the world at a very early age, so my senses seem too sensitive. Now you have also been drawn into the vortex of the world at a very early age. So-called youthful enjoyment has not been bestowed upon you, and you will have no time to take care of future youthful enjoyment because you have already been drawn into the vortex of the world. As for our depression, because of the advancement of the trend of thought of the times, it will always be depression." "Yes, regarding our depression, because our thinking is revolutionary and progressive, our nerves will never be invaded by numbness, but on the other hand, the realistic environment exposes ferocity everywhere. Therefore, this kind of depression may be a good phenomenon. My youthful outing and my original desires are no longer something I must pursue. I only want to fight for life, go to fight for life." Speaking of this, everyone was silent and there was really nothing more to say. There were indeed many pieces of advice that Brother Zhi gave me, and they were indeed unforgettable in this life. Since I recovered slightly from my illness and came out, I have been with Brother Zhi every day and listened to his instructions. Although today I discovered white hair because of an incident and made me recall everything in the past as if I had reordered an old account, this is probably a sign that I need to stand on the path of a strong will to live and fight with everything, to fight with everything. I should not entrust great expectations to mirror flowers and water moon. The power of the environment can indeed harm me, but I will never be willing to be dominated by the environment. I should conquer the environment to create what I want to create. White hair, oh, white hair, is the enlightenment of my will, the consciousness of battle.

Guidelines for Women's Life (1) Articles should be within the scope of discussions on women's issues, domestic and foreign news about women, descriptions of women's lives, essays, etc. The style is not limited. (2) Drawings should be related to women's issues to be qualified. (3) Photos should be related to women's news, women's issues, and women's lives to be qualified. Personal and group photos are very welcome. The number of words in each article should not exceed 2,000. (4) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper. (5) The number of words in each article should not exceed 2,000. (6) Do not write manuscripts horizontally, and do not write in a careless manner. Western texts that can be omitted should be omitted. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation. (7) Do not use blue ink to draw pictures, and do not use colored paper. White paper and black drawings must be used. (8) Please indicate that the manuscript should be sent to the Women's Life Editorial Department for collection. (9) Manuscripts will not be returned whether they are published or not. If they need to be returned, please state in advance and attach sufficient postage. (10) Remuneration for articles is divided into three types: 3 yuan, 2 yuan, and 1 yuan per thousand words. The same applies to drawings and photos. If there are special manuscripts, the remuneration will be calculated separately. Guidelines for Youth Corner (1) Articles should be within the scope of discussions on youth issues, domestic and foreign news about schools or students, essays, descriptions of school life, essays, etc. The style is not limited. (2) Books are limited to those related to youth issues. (3) Photos should be related to youth life (such as sports, travel, sightseeing, drama, lectures, gatherings, exhibitions, various competitions, etc.), school news, and youth movements to be qualified. Personal and group photos are welcome. (4) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper. (5) The number of words in each article should not exceed 2,000. (6) Do not write manuscripts horizontally, and do not write in a careless manner. Western texts that can be omitted should be omitted. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation. (7) Do not use blue ink to draw pictures, and do not use colored paper. White paper and black drawings must be used. (8) Please indicate that the manuscript should be sent to the Youth Corner Editorial Department. (9) Manuscripts will not be returned whether they are published or not. If they need to be returned, please state in advance and attach sufficient postage. (10) Remuneration for articles is divided into three types: 3 yuan, 2 yuan, and 1 yuan per thousand words. The same applies to each drawing and photo. If there are special manuscripts, the remuneration will be calculated separately.
